# Agent Memory

## Project Summary

- Mensura is an AGPL-3.0 open-source, local-first and self-hostable agentic development platform for professional developers and teams.
- It combines a desktop workspace (Studio), orchestration (Core), project memory (Vault), quality and policy gates (Guard), extensions (Hub), and optional voice control (Voice).
- The product emphasizes reproducible agent runs, visible diffs and logs, human approval, mandatory checks, open MCP interoperability, and user-managed model providers.
- Current implementation status: the repository has a runnable pnpm workspace, tested shared contracts, a verified FastAPI Core service, and a Tauri/React Studio flow for workspace selection -> Vault inventory -> immutable context pack -> ready task -> context-bound queued run -> explicit deterministic or optional OpenAI BYOK execution -> separately persisted bounded change proposal -> approve/reject review -> optional isolated sandbox verification of approved proposals -> explicit digest-checked apply-to-live of an approved, verified proposal -> explicit digest-guarded undo of applied applications. Verification materializes the proposal only inside a temporary detached Git worktree, runs the configured Guard checks there, persists a separate artifact with sandbox/per-file/Guard/safe-diff metadata, and removes the sandbox without writing the live branch or working tree. Apply-to-live is a separately gated action that writes the exact verified content to the live working tree with digest checks and atomic replaces, re-runs Guard on the result, and persists a separate `ApplicationArtifact` with per-file digests and undo metadata—refusing on drift before any write and never running a Git command or provider call. Undo is an explicit bounded action that consumes the recorded undo metadata (prior content and digests) to atomically restore or remove files, refusing before any write when the live tree drifted; it produces a separate `UndoArtifact` with per-file outcomes and re-runs Guard after restoration. OpenAI keys use the OS credential backend, current `review.v2` output is code-bounded, `review.v1` remains versioned, and deterministic remains credential-free. Repository/Git inspection and Vault remain read-only. Durable resource persistence, additional providers, and orchestration remain unimplemented.

## Source Documents Read

### `mensura_master_spec.md`

- Defines the product vision, module responsibilities, deployment modes, entities, technology candidates, and MVP/V1/V2 scope.
- Positions Mensura as engineering-controlled and self-host-first, with MCP-based interoperability and BYOK providers.
- Defines the target end-to-end task flow: context retrieval, agent execution, isolated changes, Guard checks, diff review, and human approval.

### `mensura_prd.md`

- Makes repository connection, persisted run history, semantic retrieval, pre-completion checks, MCP compatibility, and local/Docker deployment functional requirements.
- Defines the MVP as Studio, basic indexing, one orchestration path, diff review, lint/test integration, and BYOK.
- The central acceptance criterion is a working repo-to-agent-to-diff-to-checks-to-approval flow.

### `mensura_architecture.md`

- Establishes Studio -> Core as the primary boundary; Core coordinates Vault, Guard, provider, Git, queue, and runner adapters.
- Recommends Tauri/React for Studio and FastAPI/LangGraph for Core, with PostgreSQL, Redis, vector search, and Docker in the scaling path.
- Requires sandboxed execution where possible and durable audit records for approvals, tool calls, and risky changes.

### `mensura_roadmap.md`

- Orders delivery from monorepo and standards through Studio, Core, Vault, Guard, team mode, Hub, and advanced features.
- Keeps multi-agent swarms, Voice, remote runners, and scheduled automation out of the early MVP path.
- Treats package boundaries and coding standards as Phase 0 prerequisites.

### `mensura_agent_specs.md`

- Defines architect, research, coder, test, reviewer, security, DevOps, and docs roles.
- Requires every agent result to include summary, actions, files, rationale, risks, and next step.
- Describes role contracts, not an implementation framework or wire protocol.

### `mensura_api_outline.md`

- Lists REST boundaries for workspaces, projects, tasks, runs, Vault, Guard, and Hub.
- Lists WebSocket channels for run, task, and project events.
- Leaves request/response schemas, pagination, error envelopes, versioning, and authentication open.

### `mensura_guard_spec.md`

- Defines an ordered check pipeline from format and lint through tests, secrets, dependency checks, risk scoring, and approval.
- Requires failed tests and detected secrets to block completion.
- Requires protected paths and plugin network access to trigger explicit policy handling.

### `mensura_plugin_sdk_spec.md`

- Defines tool, MCP connector, agent, prompt, UI, and template plugin categories.
- Requires versioned manifests, explicit permissions, compatibility declarations, install review, and credential isolation.
- Names `@mensura/sdk`, `@mensura/mcp`, and `@mensura/shared-types` as public packages.

### `mensura_monorepo_structure.md`

- Defines `apps`, `services`, `packages`, `infra`, `examples`, `scripts`, and `docs` boundaries.
- Places Studio in `apps/studio` and Core/Vault/Guard/Hub/Voice in independent service directories.
- Includes shared config, SDK, MCP, prompts, types, UI, and test utilities as packages.

### `mensura_setup_guide.md`

- Declares Rust, Node LTS, pnpm, Python 3.12+, Docker Compose, and Git prerequisites.
- Describes a future setup sequence using PostgreSQL/Redis, migrations, Core, Studio, repository connection, and indexing.
- Defines the first demo as architecture summary -> small task -> coder diff -> Guard checks -> approval.

### `LICENSE`

- The repository is already licensed under GNU AGPL v3, matching the master specification's open hosted-derivative recommendation.

## Planned Architecture

### Studio

- Tauri 2 desktop shell with a React/TypeScript UI.
- Owns workspace presentation: repository tree, editor, terminal, task board, agent chat, diff review, logs, and session restoration.
- Communicates with Core through versioned HTTP contracts and WebSocket events; it should not embed orchestration or policy rules in UI code.

### Core

- FastAPI service and orchestration authority for tasks, runs, agent dispatch, context assembly, model routing, approvals, retries, and logs.
- Uses adapters for providers, Git, execution runners, Vault, and Guard so local MVP implementations can later be replaced by team-scale services.
- Starts with one explicit sequential workflow; graph orchestration and parallel agents follow only after that flow is observable and reliable.

### Vault

- Owns repository/document ingestion, chunk metadata, retrieval, project decisions, and task/run-linked memory.
- Starts with deterministic file indexing and queryable metadata; embeddings and graph relationships are added behind stable interfaces.
- Must be branch-aware before shared team memory is treated as authoritative.

### Guard

- Owns check definitions, ordered execution, structured results, blocking policy decisions, protected paths, risk signals, approvals, and audit events.
- Core requests evaluations but does not override a blocking Guard result.
- The MVP begins with configurable format/lint/test commands and explicit pass/fail/error states.

### Hub

- Owns plugin manifests, compatibility, permissions, installation metadata, signatures, connectors, templates, and agent packs.
- Post-MVP marketplace work follows a smaller local plugin loader with reviewable manifests and deny-by-default permissions.

### Voice

- Optional post-MVP adapter for local/cloud transcription and command parsing.
- Feeds normal Studio/Core commands and does not create a separate privileged execution path.

### Shared packages

- `shared-types`: versioned API entities, state machines, event payloads, errors, Guard results, and plugin manifest contracts.
- `config`: shared TypeScript, lint, formatting, and build conventions.
- `sdk`: supported plugin-facing client APIs; `mcp`: MCP adapters; `ui`: reusable Studio components; `prompts`: versioned prompt assets; `test-utils`: shared fixtures.
- Cross-service contracts remain explicit and dependency-light; services do not import each other's internal modules.

### Infra

- Local-first development scripts, Docker Compose for shared dependencies, and CI checks land before Kubernetes or Terraform.
- PostgreSQL/Redis/vector infrastructure is introduced when a working slice needs it, not as empty deployment boilerplate.
- Observability begins with structured logs and stable run IDs, then expands to OpenTelemetry and metrics.

## Current Status

- Work cycle 28 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `88f02b2`: the Studio **Vault memory** panel now visibly shows the retrieval mode, reusing **only** data Core already exposes — no Core/shared-types/schema/persistence change. A durable **retrieval-mode badge** in the summary card derives from `snapshot.summary.embedding` (`VaultEmbeddingInfo`): `Semantic search active — <backend> / <model>` (green) when `semantic` is true, `Lexical search active` (neutral) when false, and a `legacy index — re-index for semantic` variant when the optional field is absent (pre-cycle-27 index). A per-query **strategy chip** in the results meta derives from `response.strategy`: `Ranked by semantic similarity` (+ backend/model) for `semantic-cosine:*`, `Ranked by lexical similarity` for `lexical-vector-cosine`, and an amber `Lexical fallback — re-index for semantic search` for `lexical-fallback:reindex-required` (the actionable signal that the configured backend no longer matches the index). Tooltips disclose local-embeddings/no-cloud, the "results still work but relevance may be lower" fallback nuance, and that the summary badge reflects the index's build backend while the per-query mode shows with results. The stale `AboutVault` copy ("not a neural embedding model") was corrected to describe the dual semantic/lexical behavior and the re-index requirement. Backend-unavailable-during-index (`503 vault-embedding-backend-unavailable`) is already surfaced honestly by `ProblemDetailsView` on the build error — left as-is. Only `VaultIndexPanel.tsx`, its test, `styles.css`, `apps/studio/README.md`, and this journal changed. Automated: Studio `86 passed` (5 new: semantic/lexical/legacy summary badges, lexical-fallback + semantic results chips) + `tsc --noEmit` + `vite build` all green; Core and shared-types untouched. Next: an approximate-nearest-neighbor / SQLite-vector structure to keep search sub-linear as indexes grow, and feeding `POST /vault/summarize` into the context-pack/task flow.
- Work cycle 27 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `dd47b74`: Vault retrieval now ranks by real local neural embeddings behind the existing `Embedder` protocol. A new `vault_embedding.py` adds an `OllamaEmbedder` (real semantic vectors from a local Ollama daemon via `httpx` — no cloud, no new deps) alongside the offline lexical `HashingEmbedder`, both returning the same L2-normalized sparse-dict shape so the schema, the `vault_chunks.embedding` JSON column, and cosine ranking are **unchanged (no migration)**. `build_vault_embedder()` selects a backend from `MENSURA_VAULT_EMBEDDER`/`MENSURA_OLLAMA_URL`/`MENSURA_OLLAMA_EMBED_MODEL` (default `auto` → Ollama when reachable, else lexical), probes once, and logs an honest reason on fallback; only production (`create_sql_app`) probes, `create_app`/tests default to offline lexical. Search ranks by embedding cosine (primary) + exact-substring boost (secondary), reports `strategy` honestly (`semantic-cosine:ollama/<model>` | `lexical-vector-cosine` | `lexical-fallback:reindex-required`), records the producing backend in the index summary's new optional `embedding` field, fails clearly (`503 vault-embedding-backend-unavailable`) if the backend dies mid-index, and degrades to a lexical re-rank (never scoring across incompatible spaces) when an index was built by a different backend. Automated: Core `285 passed` (24 new) + ruff clean; shared-types `68 passed` + build; Studio `81 passed` + typecheck + build with **zero Studio code changes**. A live `create_sql_app()` smoke (Ollama absent) proved the honest lexical fallback + logged setup message; a deterministic demo showed semantic beating lexical on vocabulary-gap queries ("sign in" → lexical 0 hits, semantic retrieves the auth files). Ollama is not installed in this environment, so a real-model quality number is deferred; the semantic path/fallback/persistence are proven with a deterministic fake. Studio Vault UX is unchanged; surfacing the mode as a badge is the next slice.
- Work cycle 19 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `feaea03`: proposal verification, application apply, application undo, and backup creation can each run as durable, persisted background jobs. A new `jobs` table (Alembic migration `004`) stores `Job` schema-v1 records with `jobType`, polymorphic `targetEntityType`/`targetEntityId`, optional `workspaceId`, `status` (`queued | running | succeeded | failed`), `attemptCount`, a bounded reference `payload`, produced-artifact `resultEntityType`/`resultEntityId`, a bounded `lastError`, and lifecycle timestamps. Three additive endpoints (`POST /api/v1/jobs`, `GET /api/v1/jobs`, `GET /api/v1/jobs/{job_id}`) enqueue and inspect jobs; the existing synchronous verify/apply/undo/backup endpoints are unchanged. A single in-process `JobWorker` (started from the FastAPI lifespan in production, driven deterministically in tests) atomically claims the oldest queued job via a compare-and-set, invokes the exact same service method as the synchronous endpoint (preserving every digest/Guard/path/single-use safety check and adding no provider/Git capability), and persists `queued → running → succeeded|failed`. Job success means the operation produced its artifact; only pre-write refusals mark a job failed. On restart, queued jobs are drained and interrupted `running` jobs are recovered to `failed` with an honest summary; automatic retries are deferred. A compact `job.status.changed` SSE event drives a live Studio Jobs panel. Automated (153 Core tests including 29 new; 57 shared-type tests including 10 new; 69 Studio tests including 4 new, App.test.tsx fixed), Ruff lint/format, both production builds, and `cargo check` pass. Core OpenAPI now covers 42 operations across 37 paths. A live process-restart script proved recovery + queue drain end-to-end. Automatic retries, cancellation, priorities, scheduled jobs, restore-as-job, and distributed coordination remain deferred.
- Work cycle 18 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `feaea03`: Studio can receive live bounded SSE updates from Core via `GET /api/v1/events/stream` and automatically reflect status changes for run transitions, verification creation, application, undo, and backup operations without waiting for polling ticks. A compact `MensuraEvent` envelope carries only status and minimal summary (≤200 chars) — never artifact bodies, file contents, diffs, or patches. Five event types are emitted: `run.status.changed`, `verification.created`, `application.created`, `undo.created`, `backup.created`. An `InMemoryEventPublisher` with sliding buffer (last 100 events) supports `Last-Event-Id` replay. Studio's `useLiveEvents` hook subscribes via `EventSource` and invalidates relevant TanStack Query keys on each event, triggering fresh REST fetches. Existing run polling (`refetchInterval: 1_000` while `running`) is preserved as fallback. REST remains the source of truth. Automated (124 Core tests including 13 new SSE tests, 47 shared-type tests), strict TypeScript compilation, and Ruff lint/format pass. Core OpenAPI now covers 36 operations across 32 paths (new `/api/v1/events/stream`). WebSockets, bidirectional events, guaranteed durable replay, and multi-instance fanout remain deferred.
- Work cycle 17 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `feaea03`: safe local backup and restore for the Core artifact database using Python `sqlite3.Connection.backup()` API.
- Work cycle 14 is committed to `main` as `c0cb084` (from clean baseline commit `402689a`): an approved proposal with a referenced passing verification can be explicitly applied to the live working tree through `POST /api/v1/change-proposals/{id}/apply`. Application is digest-checked and all-or-nothing (validate every live digest, refuse drift/unsafe paths as RFC 9457 problems before any write, then stage fsynced temp files and atomically `os.replace`/`os.unlink`), consumes the proposal's exact verified content with no provider access, re-runs Guard on the live tree, and persists a separate reviewable `ApplicationArtifact` with a closed status (`applied_guard_passed | applied_guard_failed | applied_guard_unavailable | application_failed`), per-file digests, and undo metadata—while running no `git add`/commit/push/checkout/reset. Studio adds a gated apply action and read-only result panel below verification. Automated (88 Core + 26 shared + 65 Studio tests) plus live acceptance prove verified content reaches the live tree with no Git side effects on a demo repo, and that apply is correctly refused with zero writes on the Mensura repo (whose Guard config cannot verify inside a worktree). Undo execution remains deferred.
- Work cycle 13 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `92b773c`: approved change proposals can be verified in a temporary detached Git-worktree sandbox where materialization is digest-checked and Guard runs against the sandbox contents; a separate `ProposalVerification` artifact records sandbox/per-file/Guard/safe-diff evidence, Studio reviews it below proposal approval, and automated plus live acceptance prove the live repository is never written and sandboxes are cleaned up even on Guard failure.
- Work cycle 12 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `64d6118`: successful schema-v2 runs can materialize one separately persisted bounded `ChangeProposal`, Studio can inspect file-level digest/content metadata and record a terminal approve/reject decision, and automated plus native acceptance prove no repository application occurs.
- Work cycle 11 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `9c7bba9`: Core/Studio support redacted local OpenAI BYOK configuration, explicit deterministic/real execution selection, OS-keyring secret storage, non-secret user config, `review.v1`, and bounded locally validated structured output without widening repository or tool capabilities.
- Work cycle 10 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `ac80ea8`: queued runs can be manually executed through an injected deterministic provider using only the persisted task/context pack, with atomic explicit transitions and bounded structured result/failure review in Studio.
- Work cycle 9 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `9d63e6e`: queued run creation requires an existing immutable context pack owned by the task workspace, persists the exact binding, and Studio shows the selected and stored execution context before any provider execution.
- Work cycle 8 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `9c258d3`: Core creates deterministic immutable context packs only from an existing Vault inventory, and Studio explicitly selects and reviews their exact bounded evidence without provider execution.
- Work cycle 7 is complete in the working tree from clean baseline commit `a893268`: Core has deterministic process-local Vault inventory and bounded safe text retrieval, and Studio has a compact active-workspace inventory/preview inspector.
- Work cycle 6 is complete in the working tree from baseline commit `6552d2d`: Core has a manually triggered, bounded Ruff/pytest Guard runner and Studio has a compact active-workspace result panel.
- Core v1 now includes tested replaceable read-only Git inspection, Guard execution, Vault inventory, and immutable context-pack adapters in addition to versioned resource routes, predictable RFC 9457 errors, replaceable in-memory storage, and OpenAPI.

## Completed Work Log

### 2026-07-20 — Start work cycle 14: explicit apply-to-live with audit artifact

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Baseline: confirmed a clean worktree at commit `402689a` (cycle 13 committed) and re-read the full proposal/verification/Guard code paths — `verification_service`, `verification_models`, `verification_sandbox`, `verification_repositories`, `change_proposal_models`, `change_proposal_repositories`, `guard_execution`, `guard_config`, `guard_runner`, `git_adapter`, `models`, the problem registry/handlers, dependency wiring, `create_app`, the verifications/change-proposals routers, the shared `verification.ts` contract, and the Studio proposal/verification sections plus client/query-key seams.
- Artifact boundary: introduce `ApplicationArtifact` as a fifth artifact separate from run, proposal, Guard run, context pack, and verification. It links proposal/verification/run/task/workspace/context-pack lineage and owns live-target metadata (kind, live HEAD commit, verification commit, HEAD-moved flag), a compact bounded Guard result, per-file applied results with expected/observed/applied digests, undo metadata, an application summary, a closed status, and timestamps.
- Application strategy: explicit, digest-checked, all-or-nothing two-phase apply to the live working tree with NO Git mutation. Phase 1 resolves each safe live path (rejecting escapes/symlinked components), reads live content, and compares the observed digest against the proposal's captured before-digest; any drift/unsafe path refuses the entire application as an RFC 9457 problem before writing anything. Phase 2 stages every create/modify body to a same-directory temp file (flush+fsync), then commits atomic `os.replace`/`os.unlink`. Content is the proposal's exact digest-checked stored text, never re-generated. Invariant: an `ApplicationArtifact` exists iff the live tree was written.
- Outcome model (persisted, closed): `applied_guard_passed`, `applied_guard_failed`, `applied_guard_unavailable` (written but Guard could not execute — honestly recorded, never hidden), and `application_failed` (a rare partial write during commit, recorded per file). Pre-write refusals (missing/unapproved proposal, missing/mismatched/not-passing verification, truncated content, already-applied single-apply, non-Git or drifted live tree, unsafe path, missing Guard config) are RFC 9457 problems with no artifact and no write.
- Eligibility: proposal exists + approved + untruncated; a referenced verification that belongs to the proposal and is `passed`; no existing application for the proposal (single-apply); workspace is a usable Git repository; Guard config loads; and every live file digest still matches the verified materialization basis.
- Undo metadata only (no execution this cycle): per affected file record prior existence/digest/bounded prior text + truncation flag, applied digest, change type, and a capture timestamp so a future undo can restore text files.
- API: add `POST /api/v1/change-proposals/{proposal_id}/apply` (body `{ verificationId }`, 201 + Location), `GET /api/v1/applications/{application_id}`, and `GET /api/v1/workspaces/{workspace_id}/applications`, with new stable problems for not-approved, verification-not-found/mismatch/not-passing, content-incomplete, already-applied, in-progress, live-drift, unsafe-path, and write-failed, reusing repository/Guard problems.
- Explicitly deferred: undo execution/rollback, Git stage/add/commit/push/checkout/reset, provider access during apply, background/async apply, durable persistence, re-apply after refusal, and non-Git workspaces.
- Follow-up: define shared application contracts, extract a shared safe-path helper, implement the digest-checked atomic writer + service + APIs + tests, add the Studio apply/result UI, then run automated and live acceptance and update docs.

### 2026-07-20 — Implement and verify Core apply-to-live

- Files changed: `packages/shared-types/src/{application,application.test,index}.ts`; new Core `safe_paths.py`, `application_models.py`, `application_repositories.py`, `application_writer.py`, `git_workspace.py`, `application_service.py`, `api/routers/applications.py`; edited Core `verification_service.py`, `exceptions.py`, `api/{problems,dependencies,router}.py`, `main.py`; new `tests/test_application_api.py`; edited `tests/test_openapi.py`; and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Contracts: `ApplicationArtifact` schema `1` mirrors TypeScript/Pydantic with proposal/verification/run/task/workspace/context lineage, the closed status set (`applied_guard_passed | applied_guard_failed | applied_guard_unavailable | application_failed`), `live_working_tree` target metadata (live HEAD, verification commit, HEAD-moved flag), a compact bounded Guard result, per-file applied results with expected/live-before/after/applied digests plus a closed reason (`applied | write_failed | not_attempted`), an application summary, and undo metadata (per-file prior existence/digest/bounded prior text + truncation flag + applied digest). Coherence validators tie status, Guard presence, the unavailable reason, and the applied/failed partition together. The request body is `{ verificationId }`.
- Safe paths: extracted `resolve_safe_target` into shared `safe_paths.py`, hardened to also refuse absolute paths and `..` components, and delegated verification's `_safe_target` to it (its symlink unit test still passes).
- Writer: `apply_proposal_changes` is a pure-filesystem two-phase engine. Phase 1 plans every change, resolving the safe live path, refusing unsafe paths (`ApplicationUnsafePathError`) and any create-target-exists / missing-target / before-digest mismatch as `ApplicationLiveDriftError` before writing, and capturing bounded UTF-8 prior content (64 KiB/file cap; binary/oversized flagged truncated). Phase 2 stages every create/modify body to a same-directory `mkstemp` temp file with `flush`+`os.fsync` (staging failure → `ApplicationWriteError`, nothing live changed), then commits atomic `os.replace`/`os.unlink`; a rare mid-commit failure marks the offending file `write_failed`, the rest `not_attempted`, and returns `partial=True`. No Git command runs.
- Service: `ChangeApplicationService.apply` enforces eligibility (approved, untruncated, non-empty, a referenced verification that belongs to the proposal and is `passed`, single-apply, usable Git repo via read-only `resolve_live_head`, Guard config loads) before writing, reserves the workspace, applies, then re-runs Guard on the live tree. A post-apply `GuardError` becomes `applied_guard_unavailable` (never discards the written artifact); a partial write becomes `application_failed`; otherwise the status follows the live Guard status. Persistence is single-apply per proposal, so an artifact exists iff the live tree was written.
- API/problems: added `POST /api/v1/change-proposals/{proposal_id}/apply` (201 + Location), `GET /api/v1/applications/{application_id}`, and `GET /api/v1/workspaces/{workspace_id}/applications`, with new problems `application-not-found`, `application-proposal-not-approved`, `application-content-incomplete`, `application-empty-proposal`, `application-verification-not-found/-mismatch/-not-passed`, `application-already-exists`, `application-in-progress`, `application-live-drift`, `application-unsafe-path`, and `application-write-failed`, reusing repository/Guard problems. OpenAPI now covers 28 paths.
- Verification: Ruff lint/format pass and all 88 Core tests pass (78 prior + 10 new). New coverage proves verified content reaches the live tree with no commit/stage/push/worktree side effects, drift refusal writes nothing and persists nothing, unapproved/absent/failed-verification refusals, applied-then-Guard-failed capture, single-apply, empty-proposal refusal, Guard-config-missing pre-check refusal, and artifact retrieval/listing.
- Follow-up: add the Studio apply action/result UI gated on approved+verified+passed+not-applied, typed client/query methods, then run the full monorepo acceptance and live acceptance.

### 2026-07-20 — Implement and verify Studio apply-to-live and full acceptance

- Files changed: `apps/studio/src/api/{coreClient,coreClient.test}.ts`, `apps/studio/src/app/queryClient.ts`, `apps/studio/src/test/render.tsx`, `apps/studio/src/features/change-proposals/{ChangeProposalPanel,ProposalApplicationSection,ProposalApplicationSection.test}.tsx`, `apps/studio/src/styles.css`, root/Core/Studio READMEs, and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Client/query: typed `applyChangeProposal(proposalId, { verificationId })`, `getApplication`, and `listWorkspaceApplications` with encoded routes, plus `application` and `workspaceApplications` query keys; the test render harness stubs all three (applications list resolves empty).
- UI: `ProposalApplicationSection` renders only for approved proposals, below the verification section, so proposal/verification/application stay visibly distinct. Boundary copy frames apply as a high-trust action that writes verified content to the live working tree while never committing/staging/pushing and never calling a provider. A precondition checklist (approved, verified, verification passed, not yet applied) gates the action; the primary `Apply to live working tree` button appears only with a passing verification (reusing the shared verification-collection query, so no extra request) and names the exact verification used. The result panel shows the closed status with a tone-mapped badge, outcome copy, live-target commit + HEAD-moved flag, a per-file digest-checked write list (`liveBefore → applied`), the live Guard block or unavailable reason, and a compact undo-basis summary (prior digests + restorability, never raw prior bodies). Application is single-use, and apply RFC 9457 problems render inside the section without disabling it.
- Verification: strict Studio TypeScript, all 65 Studio tests across 17 files (6 new), and the production build pass; root `pnpm check` passes strict shared/Studio TypeScript, 26 shared tests, 65 Studio tests, both production builds, and `cargo check`.
- Docs: root/Core/Studio READMEs now describe the three apply endpoints, the `ApplicationArtifact` schema/status set, the digest-checked all-or-nothing writer, post-apply Guard, undo metadata (execution deferred), all new problems, and the Studio apply section; stale "apply remains unimplemented" language was replaced.
- Follow-up: run live acceptance against a demo repo and the Mensura repo, then close the cycle journal and current status.

### 2026-07-20 — Complete work cycle 14: apply-to-live acceptance

- Commit: the cycle landed on `main` as `c0cb084` (`feat(applications): add explicit verified apply-to-live flow`, 30 files, +2938/-20) from clean baseline `402689a`.
- Files changed this cycle: `packages/shared-types/src/{application,application.test,index}.ts`; new Core `safe_paths.py`, `application_models.py`, `application_repositories.py`, `application_writer.py`, `git_workspace.py`, `application_service.py`, `api/routers/applications.py`; edited Core `verification_service.py`, `exceptions.py`, `api/{problems,dependencies,router}.py`, `main.py`; new `tests/test_application_api.py`; edited `tests/test_openapi.py`; six Studio source/test files; root/Core/Studio READMEs; and `docs/agent_memory.md`. No dependency or lockfile changed.
- Application strategy chosen: explicit, digest-checked, all-or-nothing two-phase apply (validate every live digest → stage fsynced temp files → atomic `os.replace`/`os.unlink`) with pure-filesystem writes and zero Git commands. Live drift/unsafe path is refused as an RFC 9457 problem before any write, so the invariant is that an `ApplicationArtifact` exists iff the live tree was written. Content is the proposal's exact verified stored text; a passing verification (referenced by id) is required.
- Automated verification: root `pnpm check` passes strict TypeScript, 26 shared tests, 65 Studio tests, both production builds, and `cargo check`; Ruff lint/format and all 88 warning-strict Core tests pass; `cargo fmt --check` and `git diff --check` are clean. Core OpenAPI now covers 31 operations across 28 paths (three new apply paths).
- Live acceptance (demo repository): a real Uvicorn Core with an injected create/modify/delete draft drove workspace → inventory → pack → task → run → proposal → approve → verify (passed) → apply against a fresh temp Git repo whose committed Guard config invokes the Core venv's real Ruff and pytest. Apply returned `201`/`applied_guard_passed`; the live tree gained the modified file and new file and lost the deleted file; `git status` showed only unstaged/untracked working-tree changes (`M src/example.py`, `D src/old.py`, `?? docs/`) with HEAD, commit count, and staged set unchanged; the artifact was retrievable with prior content captured for undo; and a second apply was refused `409 application-already-exists`.
- Live acceptance (Mensura repository): the committed Guard config invokes the relative `services/core/.venv/bin/python`, which is absent from a detached verification worktree, so verification returns `500 guard-execution-failed` and no passing verification can exist. Apply on an unapproved proposal returned `409 application-proposal-not-approved`, and apply with a verification id returned `404 application-verification-not-found`; the real repository was never written—`README.md` digest, `git status --porcelain`, the single-worktree count, and the absence of the scratch path were all identical before and after.
- Cleanup: both acceptance scripts and the demo temp repository were removed; no `mensura-*` temp directories or extra worktrees remain.
- What now works end-to-end: an approved + passing-verified proposal can be explicitly applied to the live working tree; live drift is detected and blocks unsafe application before any write; writes are atomic, bounded, and all-or-nothing; Guard re-runs on the live tree and its pass/fail/unavailable outcome is surfaced honestly; a separate `ApplicationArtifact` with per-file digests and undo metadata is persisted and reviewable in Studio; and no commit/stage/push/checkout automation or provider access occurs.
- Intentionally deferred: undo execution/rollback, Git stage/commit/push/checkout/reset, provider access during apply, background/async apply, durable persistence, re-apply after refusal, multi-workspace concurrency beyond the per-workspace reservation, non-Git workspaces, and making verification pass on the Mensura repo (its Guard config's relative venv path fails inside a detached worktree).
- Next recommended slice: implement bounded, digest-guarded undo execution that restores the captured prior content/digests (and re-deletes created files) for a text-file application, refusing when live content has drifted from the recorded applied digest—turning the existing undo metadata into a safe, explicit one-step revert.

### 2026-07-20 — Start work cycle 15: durable Core persistence with SQLite

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Baseline: confirmed a clean worktree at commit `feaea03` (cycle 14 committed), and re-read all repository Protocols (CoreRepository, GuardRunRepository, VaultInventoryRepository, ContextPackRepository, ChangeProposalRepository, ProposalVerificationRepository, ApplicationRepository), all service constructors, domain models, the complete `create_app()` dependency wiring, test fixtures, and the Studio `CoreClient`/query layer.
- Design decision: use SQLite as the first durable backend via SQLAlchemy 2.0 + Alembic migrations. Keep all existing Protocol interfaces unchanged — services consume Protocols, not concrete types, so database-backed repositories slot in transparently.
- Migration strategy: add Alembic with a single descriptive, reversible initial migration (10 tables), executed explicitly at startup via `create_app(run_migrations_on_startup=True)`. Tests disable migrations and use temp SQLite databases.
- SQLite configuration: `PRAGMA foreign_keys=ON`, `journal_mode=WAL`, `synchronous=NORMAL` configured declaratively via SQLAlchemy engine events.
- Scope: replace all 7 InMemory* repositories with SQL-backed implementations. Preserve InMemory variants for test isolation. Zero API changes, zero domain model changes, zero Studio changes.
- Storage boundaries: 10 tables — workspaces, tasks, runs, guard_runs, vault_inventory_snapshots, vault_inventory_items, context_packs, change_proposals, proposal_verifications, applications. JSON columns for bounded structured payloads (RunExecutionContext, GuardSummary, ContextPackFileEntry list, ChangeProposalFileChange list, VerificationFileResult list, etc.) where the Pydantic model already defines the shape. Explicit FKs, indexed workspace_id/run_id/proposal_id columns, and consistent timestamps.
- Recovery behavior: only data persisted BEFORE restart is readable. Old in-memory runtime state is not backfilled. Studio sees workspaces and historic artifacts after restart with zero client changes.
- Explicitly deferred: Postgres support (architecture open via URL change), async/await DB access, binary/blob storage, connection pooling beyond defaults, migration of existing in-memory state, Vault item pagination, database backup/restore tooling, and provider settings persistence (already file+keyring-backed).
- Follow-up: add SQLAlchemy+Alembic deps, create persistence layer (database.py, ORM models, 7 SQL-backed repos), wire into create_app() with run_migrations_on_startup switch, update tests for temp SQLite isolation, add restart-persistence tests, and verify the full Studio flow survives a Core restart.

### 2026-07-20 — Implement Core persistence and verify restart durability

- Files changed: `services/core/pyproject.toml` (added alembic>=1.14,<2 and sqlalchemy>=2.0,<3 deps), `services/core/src/mensura_core/main.py` (rewired create_app with use_sql/run_migrations_on_startup switches, InMemory module-level default, create_sql_app factory for production), `docs/agent_memory.md`. New files: `persistence/__init__.py`, `persistence/database.py`, `persistence/models.py`, `persistence/repositories/{core,guard,vault,context_pack,change_proposal,verification,application}.py`, `migrations/{__init__,env,script.py.mako,alembic.ini,versions/001_initial_schema}.py`, `tests/test_persistence.py`. Edited: `tests/conftest.py` (InMemory injection), `tests/test_api.py` (InMemory injection for FailingRepository test).
- Database strategy: SQLite via SQLAlchemy 2.0 synchronous sessions. Default path `~/.mensura/core.db`, overridable via `MENSURA_DATABASE_URL` env var. Engine configured with `check_same_thread=False` for thread-safe access across FastAPI request handlers.
- SQLite pragma strategy: `PRAGMA foreign_keys=ON`, `PRAGMA journal_mode=WAL`, `PRAGMA synchronous=NORMAL` — configured via SQLAlchemy `event.listen(engine, "connect", ...)` making pragmas automatic on every connection. WAL mode enables concurrent reads without blocking writes; synchronous=NORMAL balances durability with performance.
- Migration strategy: Alembic with a single reversible `001_initial_schema` migration creating all 10 tables. Triggered explicitly at startup via `create_app(run_migrations_on_startup=True)`. `alembic upgrade head` → `alembic downgrade base` round-trips cleanly. The module-level `app` (InMemory) never runs migrations; production `create_sql_app()` factory enables both migrations and SQL repos.
- Schema: 10 tables — workspaces, tasks, runs, guard_runs, vault_inventory_snapshots, vault_inventory_items, context_packs, change_proposals, proposal_verifications, applications. All tables have UUID PKs, explicit FKs, timestamps (DateTime with timezone), and indexes on workspace_id/run_id/proposal_id. Unique constraints enforce single-proposal-per-run, single-apply-per-proposal, latest-only guard/inventory semantics. JSON columns for bounded structured payloads: context_pack reference, run execution, guard summary+checks, vault summary, context pack files+limits+summary, change proposal file_changes, verification sandbox+guard+file_results+safe_diff, application target+guard+file_results+summary+undo.
- Repository implementation: each of the 7 SQL-backed repos satisfies the existing Protocol interface. `SqlCoreRepository.replace_run_if_status()` and `SqlChangeProposalRepository.replace_if_status()` implement optimistic concurrency via in-place attribute mutation on the managed ORM row. Timestamp normalization (`_ensure_tz()`) adds UTC timezone info on read since SQLite stores naive datetime strings.
- Factory wiring: `create_app(run_migrations_on_startup=True, use_sql=True)` creates SQL engine + session factory and injects all 7 Sql* repos. When `run_migrations_on_startup=False` (default), no migrations run. When `use_sql=False` (default), InMemory repos are used. Direct injection of explicit InMemory repos into `create_app()` still works for test isolation. The `create_sql_app()` factory in main.py ties both flags together for production.
- Test isolation: conftest injects all 7 InMemory repos explicitly with `run_migrations_on_startup=False`, keeping existing 88 tests isolated. New `test_persistence.py` (10 tests) uses temp SQLite databases with `use_sql=True`.
- Restart verification (automated): 10 new tests in `test_persistence.py` cover — migrations create all 10 tables from scratch, downgrade reverts cleanly, workspace survives create→restart→list, task survives create→restart→get, run (queued) survives create→restart→get, change proposal lineage survives full flow (workspace→vault→pack→run→execute→proposal→restart→retrieve), verification and application tables survive restart, immutable artifact retrieval preserves exact context_pack reference fields across restart, and table-create-only bootstrap works without migrations.
- Restart verification (manual): a real Core process lifecycle test created workspace + task + inventory + context pack + queued run + execution + change proposal, then simulated restart by constructing a fresh `create_app(use_sql=True)`. All artifacts restored: workspace listed, task fetched, run at `succeeded`, context pack listed, change proposals listed. Full lineage intact across process boundaries.
- Automated verification: Ruff lint/format passes, all 98 Core tests pass (88 existing + 10 new), no regressions.
- What persisted successfully across restart: workspaces, tasks, runs (with full execution context, provider metadata, context_pack reference), guard run history, vault inventory snapshots and items, context packs (with manifests, files, digests), change proposals (with file changes, provider lineage, status), proposal verifications, and application artifacts. Studio requires zero client changes — existing `CoreClient` queries and React Query cache patterns work identically.
- Intentionally deferred: Postgres support (architecture open via SQLAlchemy URL change), async/await DB access (synchronous SQLite is honest and sufficient for local-first use), binary/blob storage (all artifacts fit in bounded JSON columns), migration of old in-memory runtime state (only future runs are durable, no fake backfill), connection pooling beyond SQLAlchemy defaults, database backup/restore tooling, Vault item pagination, and provider settings persistence (already file-backed via JsonProviderSettingsRepository + KeyringCredentialStore).
- What now works end-to-end across restart: create workspace → create task → build inventory → create context pack → queue run → execute run → materialize proposal → restart Core → list workspaces shows persisted data → get task/run/proposal returns complete results → context packs remain retrievable → Studio can reconnect and continue.
- Next recommended slice: implement bounded, digest-guarded undo execution that restores the captured prior content/digests for a text-file application — turning the existing undo metadata into a safe, explicit one-step revert.

### 2026-07-20 — Start work cycle 13: isolated proposal verification sandbox

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Baseline: confirmed a clean worktree at commit `92b773c` (cycle 12 committed), and re-read the proposal models/service/repositories, Guard config/runner/service, Git adapter, problem handlers, dependency wiring, and `create_app` composition.
- Artifact boundary: introduce `ProposalVerification` as a fourth artifact separate from run, proposal, Guard run, and context pack. It links proposal/run/task/workspace/context-pack lineage and owns sandbox metadata, per-file materialization results, a compact bounded Guard summary, safe diff aggregates, and a closed outcome.
- Sandbox strategy: Git-worktree-first and Git-worktree-only. A temporary detached worktree of `HEAD` is created under a fresh system temp directory outside the repository, materialization happens only inside it, and cleanup (`git worktree remove --force` plus prune and temp-dir removal) is explicit; failed cleanup is recorded as safe artifact metadata, not leaked paths. Non-Git workspaces are rejected with existing repository problems instead of adding a copy fallback.
- Materialization boundary: only approved proposals with complete (untruncated) stored text are eligible. Create/modify/delete apply bounded text against digest-checked targets inside the resolved sandbox root; path escape, symlinked parents, and digest mismatches mark file results unapplied instead of writing. No commit, push, stage, or live-branch write exists anywhere in the flow.
- Guard boundary: extract the check-execution loop from `GuardService` into a shared `guard_execution` helper so verification can run the same bounded Ruff/pytest checks against the sandbox without touching the per-workspace latest-Guard-run storage or coupling to the Guard API domain.
- API boundary: add `POST /api/v1/change-proposals/{proposal_id}/verify`, `GET /api/v1/change-proposals/{proposal_id}/verifications`, and `GET /api/v1/verifications/{verification_id}` with stable RFC 9457 problems for unapproved proposals, unsupported repositories, incomplete stored content, sandbox failure, concurrent verification, and missing artifacts.
- Explicitly deferred: final apply-to-live, provider write access, commits/pushes, persistent sandboxes, non-Git fallbacks, background/async verification, and durable artifact persistence.
- Follow-up: define the shared verification contracts, then implement sandbox, materialization, Guard integration, APIs, tests, and the Studio verification UI.

### 2026-07-20 — Implement and verify Core proposal verification

- Files changed: `packages/shared-types/src/{verification,verification.test,index}.ts`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/{guard_execution,guard_service,verification_models,verification_sandbox,verification_repositories,verification_service,exceptions,main}.py`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/api/{dependencies,problems,router}.py`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/api/routers/verifications.py`, `services/core/tests/{test_verification_api,test_openapi}.py`, and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Contracts: `ProposalVerification` schema `1` mirrors TypeScript/Pydantic with proposal/run/task/workspace/context lineage, `passed | failed` status, closed `sandbox_verified | guard_failed | materialization_failed` outcomes, `git_worktree` sandbox metadata (commit, cleanup flag, no paths), per-file results with a closed reason vocabulary and digests, a compact bounded Guard result (2,000-char output excerpts), and safe diff aggregates.
- Guard extraction: the check-execution loop moved from `GuardService` into `guard_execution.execute_guard_checks`; the Guard API domain behavior, latest-run storage, and configuration/tool validation are unchanged and all previous Guard tests still pass.
- Sandbox: `GitWorktreeSandboxFactory` validates the workspace repository exactly like the read-only inspector, then creates a detached `HEAD` worktree under a fresh `mensura-verification-*` system temp directory. Cleanup runs `git worktree remove --force`, temp-dir removal, and `worktree prune` in a `finally` block; incomplete cleanup is a logged, safe artifact flag.
- Materialization: only approved untruncated proposals proceed. Symlinked path components are refused, create targets must be absent, and modify/delete targets must match the captured before digest; failures become unapplied file results (skipping Guard) instead of exceptions, and a workspace-level reservation rejects concurrent verifications.
- API: `POST /api/v1/change-proposals/{proposal_id}/verify` (201 + Location), `GET /api/v1/change-proposals/{proposal_id}/verifications`, and `GET /api/v1/verifications/{verification_id}`, with new problems `verification-not-found`, `verification-proposal-not-approved`, `verification-content-incomplete`, `verification-in-progress`, and `verification-sandbox-failed`, plus reused repository/Guard problems. OpenAPI now covers 25 paths.
- Verification: Ruff lint/format pass and all 78 Core tests pass, including sandbox success with live-tree/worktree-count invariance, unapproved/missing rejection, guard-failure capture, drifted-target materialization failure, non-Git refusal, injected sandbox-creation failure, truncated-content refusal, cleanup after missing Guard config, and symlink-refusal unit coverage.
- Follow-up: add the Studio verification action/review UI and typed client methods, then run the full monorepo acceptance.

### 2026-07-19 — Start work cycle 12: write-isolated change proposals

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Baseline: confirmed a clean worktree at commit `64d6118`, re-read the twelfth-cycle request and current immutable context/provider execution boundaries, and repeated the all-history recon over 12 commits. The history has no fix/revert magnets; documentation, Studio transport/styling, and Core bootstrap/OpenAPI remain the main integration hotspots in this young repository.
- Artifact boundary: introduce `ChangeProposal` as a resource independent of run execution state. It retains source run, task, workspace, exact `contextPackId`, provider, and prompt lineage while owning only its own review state.
- Creation boundary: proposals may be created only from persisted `succeeded` runs with a valid bounded execution result. Generation must use that stored result/context lineage and cannot receive a workspace root, live filesystem/Git/subprocess/tool/write capability, or repository content beyond already persisted bounded evidence.
- Content boundary: use a small schema with bounded summary/rationale and deterministically ordered file-change entries. File paths and proposed text are validated and bounded; binary bodies, raw unbounded patches, shell operations, and repository mutation remain absent.
- Review boundary: allow only `proposed -> approved` or `proposed -> rejected`. Review timestamps and state belong to the proposal, and repeated/conflicting review actions return stable RFC 9457 problems without mutating the source run.
- Studio boundary: add explicit proposal creation to successful-run views and a compact review panel with lineage, safe file-level content, status, and approve/reject actions. Copy must make clear that review does not apply changes.
- Explicitly deferred: patch generation/application, repository writes, Git stage/commit/checkout/reset, provider tools, live repository rereads for proposal generation, Guard-on-proposal, background jobs, SSE, retries, orchestration, and durable process-restart persistence.

### 2026-07-19 — Define and verify change-proposal contracts

- Files changed: `packages/shared-types/src/{change-proposal,change-proposal.test,execution,execution.test,provider,provider.test,index}.ts` and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Versioning: successful provider output advances to execution schema `2` and `review.v2`; the existing `review.v1` identifier remains defined rather than being silently reinterpreted. Schema v2 adds one immutable `proposalDraft` with summary, rationale, and bounded create/modify/delete suggestions.
- Artifact contract: `ChangeProposal` schema `1` is separate from `Run` and records UUID identity, source run/task/workspace, exact context-pack digest, provider/prompt lineage, proposed/approved/rejected review state, timestamps, summary/rationale, and safe per-file metadata.
- Content contract: file changes carry normalized path, closed change type, optional language, Core-derived before/after digests, bounded proposed text, stored/original byte counts, and an explicit truncation flag. Checked-in limits cap changes at 16, source text at 128 KiB, stored text at 8 KiB/file and 32 KiB/proposal.
- Lifecycle: only proposal review state is mutable; the source run result remains a terminal immutable draft and contains no approval state. The intended Core transitions remain exactly `proposed -> approved | rejected`.
- Verification: strict shared TypeScript checking and all 22 tests across eight files pass.
- Follow-up: implement Pydantic parity, `review.v2` provider validation, an idempotent in-memory proposal repository, safe draft materialization, state transitions, RFC 9457 mappings, and versioned routes.

### 2026-07-19 — Implement and verify Core change proposals

- Files changed: `services/core/src/mensura_core/{models,provider_adapter,provider_prompts,openai_provider,provider_registry,change_proposal_models,change_proposal_repositories,change_proposal_service,exceptions,main}.py`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/api/{dependencies,problems,router}.py`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/api/routers/change_proposals.py`, `services/core/tests/{test_change_proposal_api,test_provider_api,test_run_execution,test_openapi}.py`, and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Execution evolution: `review.v2` is a new code-controlled mapping that asks for a compact proposal draft grounded only in the persisted task and exact immutable context pack. OpenAI strict JSON Schema plus local Pydantic validation cover the draft; the deterministic provider emits an explicit empty-change draft instead of fabricating code. The adapter input still has no workspace root, filesystem, Git, shell, tool, or write capability.
- Artifact architecture: `ChangeProposalService` depends only on read access to process-local task/run/context records and a dedicated proposal repository. It performs no provider call and receives no live repository capability. `InMemoryChangeProposalRepository` stores one idempotent artifact per run and supports atomic expected-state review replacement.
- Materialization: only a persisted `succeeded` run with result schema `2` is eligible. Core rechecks task/run/context lineage, validates normalized relative paths and create/modify/delete semantics against the immutable manifest, derives before digests from captured entries and after digests from the complete proposal text, sorts changes deterministically, and never accepts binary text bodies.
- Bounds: source proposal text is capped at 128 KiB. Stored text is UTF-8-safe truncated to 8 KiB/file and 32 KiB/artifact, while original/stored byte counts and truncation remain explicit; after digests cover the complete pre-truncation suggestion. Oversized aggregate output returns 413 and malformed semantic output returns 422.
- API: added `POST /api/v1/runs/{run_id}/change-proposals`, `GET /api/v1/change-proposals/{proposal_id}`, `GET /api/v1/workspaces/{workspace_id}/change-proposals`, `POST /api/v1/change-proposals/{proposal_id}/approve`, and `POST /api/v1/change-proposals/{proposal_id}/reject`. Creation returns `{ proposal, created }` plus `Location`; repeated creation returns the exact stored artifact with `created: false`.
- Errors/lifecycle: stable RFC 9457 types cover absent proposal, ineligible run, malformed provider proposal, oversized content, and invalid repeated/conflicting review. Only `proposed -> approved | rejected` is allowed; source run state never changes.
- Verification: Ruff lint/format pass and all 68 Core tests pass with warnings treated as errors. Coverage proves successful/idempotent creation, get/list, immutable lineage/digests, no file mutation, queued/missing-run rejection, approve/reject terminality, UTF-8 truncation, aggregate oversize refusal, traversal refusal, updated provider schema, and OpenAPI surface/bounds.
- Follow-up: add typed Studio client/query methods and a reusable successful-run proposal panel with creation, lineage/content review, explicit approve/reject actions, bounded display, and clear non-application copy.

### 2026-07-19 — Define and verify provider selection contracts

- Files changed: `packages/shared-types/src/{provider,provider.test,execution,execution.test,index}.ts` and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Provider contract: the v1 provider set is deliberately closed to `mensura.builtin` and `openai`. Descriptors expose a human name, `deterministic | real` kind, configured state, nullable model, and prompt version; they never contain credentials. The OpenAI configuration request marks `apiKey` as write-only, and execution accepts one explicit `providerId`.
- Execution metadata: persisted provider identity now also records `providerKind` and `promptVersion`. The sole prompt version is `review.v1`; both deterministic and real executions therefore remain reviewable against a code-controlled contract.
- Fallback rule: deterministic is the visible default and always available without configuration. Core will not silently replace a selected OpenAI execution after a configuration or upstream failure, because that would make persisted provider intent misleading.

### 2026-07-19 — Prepare Core BYOK configuration and OpenAI adapter

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Storage plan: persist only OpenAI's model identifier in a small user-config JSON file outside the workspace; store the API key under a fixed Mensura service/account in the operating-system credential backend through Python `keyring`. Both boundaries are protocols with in-memory test adapters, and read APIs return only configured/model state.
- Adapter plan: call the OpenAI Responses API directly with `httpx`, `store: false`, no tools, a bounded output-token limit, and strict JSON Schema output. The adapter will independently parse and validate a smaller vendor payload, then combine it with Core-derived immutable context aggregates into the existing result schema.
- Prompt plan: `review.v1` is an explicit code mapping that serializes only the stored task and exact immutable manifest, including bounded captured previews; it has no workspace root, live file lookup, Git, shell, tool, or write channel.
- Selection plan: a provider registry resolves the requested ID before claiming the queued run. Unsupported or unconfigured providers leave the run queued. Once claimed, credential rejection, upstream failure, or invalid structured output ends the run as a bounded failed terminal record and returns a dedicated RFC 9457 problem.
- Follow-up: implement the Core models/storage/registry/prompt/adapter/service/routes/problems, install the two small runtime dependencies, and pass Ruff plus the full warning-strict Core suite.

### 2026-07-19 — Implement and verify Core optional OpenAI BYOK execution

- Files changed: `services/core/pyproject.toml`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/{models,exceptions,provider_adapter,provider_prompts,provider_config,provider_registry,openai_provider,service,main}.py`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/api/{dependencies,problems,router}.py`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/api/routers/{providers,runs}.py`, `services/core/tests/{test_provider_api,test_run_execution,test_openapi}.py`, and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Provider architecture: `ProviderRegistry` now resolves an explicit execution selection and retains an injectable deterministic adapter. `mensura.builtin` is always configured; `openai` is created only from the saved model plus a retrievable local credential. Resolution happens before the atomic queued-run claim, so unsupported or unconfigured selections leave the run untouched.
- BYOK storage: `JsonProviderSettingsRepository` stores schema-v1 non-secret model settings in the platform user-config directory (or `MENSURA_CONFIG_DIR`) using an atomic `0600` file. `KeyringCredentialStore` stores the write-only key as service `dev.mensura.studio`, account `openai-api-key`, through the operating-system backend. Tests use in-memory adapters and prove the JSON/read APIs contain no key.
- Prompt/output boundary: `review.v1` is a frozen instruction/input mapping over only Task plus the exact `ContextPackManifest`. `OpenAIReviewProvider` calls `POST /v1/responses` through an injectable transport with `store: false`, no tools, a 1,200-token maximum, and strict JSON Schema. It locally validates a compact vendor result, then attaches Core-derived immutable context aggregates; it never receives a workspace/root/filesystem/Git/shell/write capability.
- API: added `GET /api/v1/providers`, `PUT /api/v1/providers/openai/config`, and a required `{ providerId }` body on `POST /api/v1/runs/{run_id}/execute`. Provider reads are redacted. Stable problems cover unsupported provider, missing/unavailable configuration, rejected credentials, upstream failure, generic adapter failure, and invalid structured result.
- Failure semantics: unsupported/unconfigured selection keeps the run queued. Once OpenAI execution is claimed, rejected credentials, upstream failures, and invalid results persist a failed run with a closed safe failure code/summary before returning RFC 9457 details. Selected OpenAI executions never silently fall back to deterministic.
- Verification: installed `keyring 25.7.0`; Ruff lint/format pass and all 63 Core tests pass with warnings treated as errors. Tests assert exact provider/prompt metadata, strict/no-tool/no-root payload behavior, local output validation, redaction, deterministic availability, and persisted terminal failures.

### 2026-07-19 — Define and verify the run execution v1 shared contract

- Files changed: `packages/shared-types/src/{domain,execution,execution.test,index,state-machine,state-machine.test,context-pack.test}.ts` and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- State contract: the actual v1 run lifecycle is now exactly `queued -> running -> succeeded | failed`. The earlier planning/checking/approval names were aspirational shared-only states with no Core behavior; removing them makes the public contract match the first real persisted execution state machine.
- Execution contract: each run has a nullable `execution` envelope. Once execution begins it records vendor-neutral provider/adapter identity; terminal records add bounded duration plus exactly one structured result or structured failure. Results pin schema version `1` and contain task summary, interpreted intent, immutable context aggregates/languages, warnings, and recommended next steps—never raw logs, prompts, patches, or repository content.
- Failure contract: terminal failures use the closed codes `provider_execution_failed` and `structured_result_invalid` plus one bounded safe summary. Provider implementation exceptions and schema validation details are not part of the public wire shape.
- Verification: strict shared TypeScript checking and all 18 tests across six files pass, including exact lifecycle transitions and a representative provider/result envelope.
- Follow-up: add Core Pydantic execution models, compare-and-set run replacement, typed provider request/output boundaries, deterministic adapter, validation/failure mapping, execute route, and focused API/state tests.

### 2026-07-19 — Prepare the Core manual execution step

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Provider plan: isolate provider identity/request/output behind a protocol. The built-in deterministic review adapter receives a frozen task input and the exact immutable context-pack manifest plus fixed limits; it derives compact intent/context/warnings/next steps without filesystem, Git, subprocess, network, or credential access.
- Persistence plan: extend the replaceable Core repository with an atomic expected-status run replacement. Core first persists `running` with `startedAt` and adapter identity, then persists either `succeeded` plus validated result or `failed` plus bounded failure and `finishedAt`; this prevents two manual requests from claiming the same queued run.
- Integrity plan: execution resolves the stored task and manifest, then checks direct binding id, task/workspace ownership, inventory/schema identity, and stored aggregate reference before invoking the provider. Missing bindings and inconsistent persisted ownership are separate stable conflicts.
- Error plan: non-queued execution, missing binding, inconsistent context, provider failure, and invalid structured output receive dedicated RFC 9457 problems. Provider/output failures still leave a readable failed run record; raw exception or validation details never cross the API.
- Test plan: cover success, persisted running/terminal transitions and timestamps, repeat/invalid state, missing run, missing bound pack, ownership inconsistency, provider exception, invalid output, compare-and-set behavior, GET persistence, and exact OpenAPI shape.
- Follow-up: implement the isolated models/adapter/service/repository/router/problems and pass Ruff plus the full warning-strict Core suite.

### 2026-07-19 — Implement and verify Core manual bounded execution

- Files changed: `services/core/src/mensura_core/{models,provider_adapter,repositories,service,main,exceptions}.py`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/api/{problems,routers/runs}.py`, `services/core/tests/{test_api,test_openapi,test_run_execution}.py`, and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Provider abstraction: `ProviderAdapter` exposes immutable provider identity plus a typed `ProviderExecutionRequest -> RunExecutionResult` operation. The request contains the stored Task and exact `ContextPackManifest`; it has no workspace root, repository/Git/filesystem handle, shell, network client, credential, or write method. `create_app` injects the adapter, defaulting to credential-free `DeterministicReviewProvider`.
- Placeholder behavior: the built-in adapter derives bounded task intent, exact context aggregates/languages, deterministic warnings for absent descriptions/binary metadata/truncated previews, and two review-oriented next steps. It never reads live files or returns preview bodies/raw logs.
- State/persistence: `InMemoryCoreRepository.replace_run_if_status` provides an atomic expected-state update. Core revalidates task/binding/manifest identity and stored aggregate evidence, claims `queued -> running` with `startedAt` and adapter identity, then writes `succeeded` with result or `failed` with safe failure plus `finishedAt` and bounded duration. A second claim cannot execute the same queued record.
- API/errors: added bodyless `POST /api/v1/runs/{run_id}/execute`. Missing run remains `404 resource-not-found`; non-queued state, missing bound manifest, and inconsistent ownership/evidence are dedicated `409` problems; provider exceptions and structured-result validation failures are dedicated `502` problems. Failed attempts remain inspectable through GET and never expose raw exception/schema details.

Task/run/pack workspace plus id/inventory/schema/aggregate evidence are rechecked before the running claim. Repeat execution, missing packs, and inconsistent bindings never invoke the provider.

Provider and result-validation exceptions persist a safe failed record and return dedicated `502` RFC 9457 problems without leaking internals; invalid state/context uses dedicated `409` problems.

### 2026-07-19 — Start work cycle 8: immutable context packs

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Baseline: confirmed clean worktree at `9c258d3`; re-read the cycle request, current journal, Vault models/service/store, Core dependency/router wiring, Studio Vault/client/App patterns, and the eight-commit history. History has no bug-fix magnets or firefighting commits; current hotspots are the expected journal, README, shared export, and Studio integration seams.
- Contract boundary: add isolated context-pack v1 contracts for create request/response, immutable manifest, deterministic file entries, summary, and collection. A pack belongs to one workspace and one concrete Vault inventory snapshot; it is not a provider payload, prompt, semantic retrieval result, task mutation, or run transition.
- Immutability boundary: accept an explicit non-empty file-path set, canonicalize and sort it, reject duplicates and paths absent from the latest inventory, capture current safe metadata plus bounded UTF-8 preview evidence, and store the complete manifest by content-derived identity. No update/delete endpoint will exist.
- Binary policy: permit binary inventory items as metadata-only entries with a content SHA-256 computed from a bounded-inventory file (maximum 5 MiB), zero preview bytes, no text field, and explicit `binary` kind. Text entries capture at most 16 KiB of UTF-8 preview plus total bytes and truncation state.
- Deterministic identity: compute per-file SHA-256 from current full file bytes; hash canonical JSON containing a schema version, workspace id, inventory id, deterministic ordered entries, limits, and aggregate summary. Exclude creation time and pack id from the digest input; repeated creation from unchanged selected inputs yields the same `sha256:<hex>` id/digest and idempotently reuses the stored manifest.
- Explicit limits: at most 50 selected files, at most 16 KiB preview per text file, and at most 256 KiB aggregate captured preview text. Vault's existing 5 MiB included-file ceiling remains the maximum hash input per file. Reject an oversized selection/aggregate rather than silently omit selected evidence.
- API boundary: synchronous `POST /api/v1/workspaces/{workspace_id}/context-packs`, `GET .../context-packs`, and `GET .../context-packs/{context_pack_id}`. List returns immutable manifest summaries only; get returns the exact manifest. Stable RFC 9457 problems cover absent inventory, invalid/excluded selections, oversized requests, changed/unavailable files, and missing packs.
- Studio boundary: add one active-workspace review panel that reuses the Vault file collection query, shows explicit checkbox selection and an upper-bound preview estimate before creation, submits via a TanStack mutation, lists process-local packs, and opens one immutable manifest without displaying full captured contents. Errors stay local to this panel.
- Explicitly deferred: provider/model execution, prompts, embeddings, semantic retrieval, editable packs, repository writes, background refresh/watchers, durable storage, task/run attachment, provider payload formats, and full content rendering.
- Follow-up: define and verify shared TypeScript contracts before implementing Core storage and hashing.

### 2026-07-19 — Define and verify the context-pack v1 shared contract

- Files changed: `packages/shared-types/src/{context-pack,context-pack.test,index}.ts` and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Defined: pinned schema version `1`; explicit `text_preview | metadata_only` capture modes; SHA-256 digest strings; manifest limits; deterministic file entries with content digest and nullable bounded preview; aggregate file/byte/truncation summary; create request/response; and summary collection contracts.
- Isolation: context-pack types live separately from Vault snapshots and task/run entities. They reference a workspace and inventory by id but do not mutate either contract or imply provider/prompt attachment.
- Binary policy is visible on the wire: binary entries remain reviewable metadata with a content digest, null text/encoding, zero preview bytes, and `metadata_only` capture mode.
- Verification: strict TypeScript typecheck/build and all 16 shared tests across five files pass.

### 2026-07-19 — Prepare the Core context-pack step

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Planned modules: isolated Pydantic context-pack models, a lock-protected immutable repository protocol/adapter, application service, router, dependency wiring, RFC 9457 exceptions/handlers, and API/OpenAPI tests. Existing Vault builder/store remains the authority for which paths are selectable.
- Capture algorithm: load the latest inventory record; normalize, de-duplicate, and sort requested POSIX paths; require every path in that exact snapshot; re-resolve each target under the workspace with the same no-symlink/containment checks; stream-hash at most Vault's allowed 5 MiB; decode at most 16 KiB of text using the existing safe preview behavior; and retain binary files as metadata-only.
- Canonicalization: Pydantic models serialize camelCase JSON; a separate digest payload omits only `id`/`digest`, uses sorted object keys and compact UTF-8 JSON separators, and retains the ordered file array. The resulting `sha256:<hex>` is both resource id and digest.
- Store semantics: `save_if_absent` never replaces a manifest and returns whether this process created it. Listing is sorted by id and returns summaries; storage remains process-local and is explicitly documented as non-durable.
- API/problems: POST returns the typed `{ contextPack, created }` envelope and a deterministic `Location`; repeated creation returns the same manifest with `created: false`. Add problem identities for invalid selection, excluded/changed files, oversized request, and missing pack; reuse missing workspace and inventory-not-built problems where exact semantics already match.
- Follow-up: implement and verify Core before changing Studio.

### 2026-07-19 — Implement and verify immutable Core context packs

- Files changed: `services/core/src/mensura_core/{context_pack_models,context_pack_repositories,context_pack_service,exceptions,main}.py`, `services/core/src/mensura_core/api/{dependencies,problems,router,routers/context_packs}.py`, `services/core/tests/{test_context_pack_api,test_openapi}.py`, and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Architecture: `ContextPackService` depends on the existing Core workspace repository, the same injected latest-inventory repository used by `VaultService`, and a separate immutable repository protocol. The default adapter stores manifests process-locally under `(workspaceId, digest)` and only supports save-if-absent, list, and get.
- Creation behavior: requires a built inventory and 1–50 unique normalized POSIX paths; sorts paths case-insensitively with an exact tie-break; rejects missing/excluded/traversing paths; rechecks root containment, every symlink component, regular-file state, current size, and Vault's 5 MiB ceiling before capture.
- Exact evidence: streams every allowed file through SHA-256 without retaining full content; text entries capture at most 16 KiB of strict UTF-8 without splitting a trailing code point; binary entries retain only metadata and digest. Any size/classification/unavailability drift produces a `409` and asks the client to refresh inventory.
- Limits: aggregate text preview bytes may not exceed 256 KiB. The service rejects the whole request with `413` if either the 50-file or aggregate-preview limit is exceeded; it never silently drops selected evidence.
- Identity: canonical compact UTF-8 JSON uses sorted object keys and contains schema/workspace/inventory ids, explicit limits, aggregate summary, and deterministically ordered complete entries. SHA-256 of this payload becomes both `id` and `digest`; creation time is absent, so identical unchanged selection against one inventory produces byte-identical manifests and idempotent storage.
- API: added POST/list/get workspace-scoped routes. POST returns `{ contextPack, created }`, always sets a deterministic `Location`, and reports `created: false` with the exact stored manifest on duplicate content. No update/delete route exists.
- Problems: added stable context-pack invalid-selection (422), too-large (413), changed-file (409), and not-found (404) RFC 9457 types; reused existing missing workspace/inventory, Vault path-invalid, and Vault excluded-file types where semantics are identical.
- Verification: Ruff lint/format pass and all 47 Core tests pass with warnings treated as errors. Coverage includes deterministic reversed-order creation, same input/same id, per-file hashes, binary metadata-only behavior, UTF-8 truncation, both limit classes, path/exclusion/duplicate/drift failures, missing inventory/workspace/pack, list/get, camelCase schemas, and exact endpoint surface.
- Follow-up: add the typed Studio client/query/mutation and a compact explicit selection/immutable-review panel without task/run attachment.

### 2026-07-19 — Tighten a generated-artifact rule found during native acceptance

- Files changed before implementation: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Observation: the release Tauri build creates ignored schema output under `apps/*/src-tauri/gen`; the current fixed Vault traversal offered those files as selectable context because general `.gitignore` interpretation is intentionally deferred.
- Decision: add one explicit case-insensitive `src-tauri/gen` directory-path exclusion, count each pruned directory once, and apply the same rule to direct context-pack selection validation. Do not add a broad `gen` directory exclusion that could hide legitimate source.
- Verification plan: add the synthetic Tauri path to the existing Vault fixture, keep included-file expectations unchanged, increment excluded count once, rerun Core/full checks, and confirm a rebuilt real Mensura inventory no longer returns any `/src-tauri/gen/` path.

- Implemented: traversal and direct relative-path checks now prune only directory paths ending in the case-insensitive pair `src-tauri/gen`; a generic directory named `gen` remains eligible. The directory counts once and its generated schemas are never enumerated or selectable by a context pack.
- Verification: Ruff lint/format and all 47 Core tests pass with warnings as errors. A direct rebuild over the real repository reports 149 included/23 excluded entries and zero paths containing `/src-tauri/gen/`.
