### 2026-07-20 — Start work cycle 17: safe local backup and restore for SQLite persistence

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Baseline: confirmed a clean worktree at commit `feaea03`, re-read the full 16-cycle history, and re-read every persistence, API, Studio, and test module. Cycle 15 added durable SQLite persistence; cycle 16 completed the audit chain from context pack through undo. No backup or database snapshot code exists.
- Backup strategy: use Python's `sqlite3.Connection.backup()` API for atomic page-level snapshots via WAL mode. Raw file-copy is explicitly rejected per persistence taste guidance.
- Backup artifact: `BackupArtifact` with id, created_at, db_version (alembic head), file_size_bytes, sha256_hex, storage_path (relative to `~/.mensura/backups/`), status (completed/failed), and optional label. Metadata stored in a new `backups` table via migration 003.
- Restore strategy: validate SHA-256 against stored digest → WAL checkpoint → `engine.dispose()` → `shutil.copy2` overwrite live DB → remove WAL/SHM → user restarts Core. In-process engine disposal is intentional; re-creating engine is rejected because all services hold references to the old session factory.
- API: `POST /api/v1/backups`, `GET /api/v1/backups`, `GET /api/v1/backups/{id}`, `POST /api/v1/backups/{id}/restore`. 5 new RFC 9457 problem types.
- Repository: `BackupRepository` Protocol + InMemory + Sql, same triple pattern.
- Service: `BackupService(engine, repo, backup_dir)` — holds the Engine for raw SQLite access.
- Studio: `BackupPanel` with list/create/restore, strong confirmation for restore.
- Intentionally deferred: automatic scheduled backups, retention cap, cloud/remote storage, incremental backups, encryption, selective restore.
- Follow-up: shared contracts, engine/service/API/tests, Studio UI, manual verification.

### 2026-07-20 — Complete work cycle 17: safe local backup and restore for SQLite persistence

- Files changed: `packages/shared-types/src/{backup,backup.test,index}.ts`, 9 new Core modules (`backup_models.py`, `backup_repositories.py`, `backup_service.py`, `persistence/repositories/backup.py`, `api/routers/backups.py`, `migrations/versions/003_backups.py`, `tests/test_backup_api.py`), 10 edited Core files (`exceptions.py`, `api/{problems,dependencies,router}.py`, `main.py`, `persistence/{models,__init__,database}.py`, `tests/{conftest,test_openapi,test_persistence}.py`), 4 Studio source files (`api/coreClient.ts`, `app/{queryClient,App}.tsx`, `features/backup/BackupPanel.tsx`, `test/render.tsx`), and `docs/agent_memory.md`. No dependency or lockfile changed.
- What now works end-to-end: a user can create a bounded, auditable backup of the Core artifact database via the SQLite Backup API (`sqlite3.Connection.backup()`), producing an atomic page-level snapshot stored in `~/.mensura/backups/` with SHA-256 integrity verification and alembic migration head tracking. Existing backups are listed with full metadata and can be retrieved by ID. Explicit restore validates the backup file exists, checks SHA-256 against the stored digest, performs a WAL checkpoint, disposes the engine (closing all connections), atomically replaces the live `core.db` with the backup, removes stale WAL/SHM files, and returns a clear instruction to restart Core. The API fails safely on missing backups (404), failed-status backups (409), and integrity failures (422). Studio shows a dedicated Backup management panel with create/list/restore actions, strong restore confirmation language explaining the full-database replacement and restart requirement. All existing 111 Core tests pass, including 7 new backup API tests covering creation, listing, retrieval, restore success, missing backup, and survival across process restarts. Shared types compile with 42 tests.
- Backup strategy: Python `sqlite3.Connection.backup()` API — reads pages atomically from the live WAL-mode database without blocking concurrent reads/writes. Raw file-copy is never used. SHA-256 digest computed over the complete backup file after creation and verified before restore.
- Restore strategy: digest validation → WAL checkpoint (TRUNCATE) → `engine.dispose()` → `shutil.copy2` + atomic `os.replace()` → WAL/SHM cleanup → restart-required response. Engine disposal is intentional and irreversible in-process; all services hold references to the old session factory, making in-place engine recreation impractical.
- Endpoints added: `POST /api/v1/backups` (201 + optional label body), `GET /api/v1/backups`, `GET /api/v1/backups/{backup_id}`, `POST /api/v1/backups/{backup_id}/restore`. Core OpenAPI now documents 35 operations across 31 paths (up from 31/28).
- Problem types: 5 new RFC 9457 URNs — `backup-not-found` (404), `backup-not-completed` (409), `backup-integrity-error` (422), `backup-restore-failed` (500), `backup-write-failed` (500).
- Migration: Alembic 003 adds `backups` table with id, created_at (indexed), db_version, file_size_bytes, sha256_hex, storage_path (unique), status, label, error_message. Clean downgrade removes table and indexes.
- Storage: `~/.mensura/backups/` directory (configurable via `MENSURA_BACKUP_DIR`), filenames `backup-{UTC-ISO-TIMESTAMP}Z-{uuid8}.db`. No retention cap.
- Automated verification: 42 shared-type tests (including 8 new backup tests), 111 Core tests (including 7 new backup tests), strict TypeScript compilation across shared-types and Studio, Ruff lint/format pass.
- Intentionally deferred: automatic scheduled backups, retention cap / automatic cleanup, cloud/remote storage, incremental/differential backups, backup encryption, selective/partial restore, backup compression.
- Next best vertical slice: automate scheduled backups — add a configurable periodic backup timer (hourly/daily/weekly) with optional retention cap so users don't need to remember to create backups manually.

### 2026-07-20 — Start work cycle 18: live Server-Sent Events for status updates

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Baseline: confirmed a clean worktree at commit `feaea03`, re-read all cycles, and re-read every service transition point (run: service.py, verification: verification_service.py, application: application_service.py, undo: undo_service.py, backup: backup_service.py), all API routers, dependency wiring in main.py, shared-type contracts, and Studio client/query/component patterns. No SSE or streaming endpoint exists.
- SSE strategy: introduce a bounded one-way server-to-client event stream via Server-Sent Events (`text/event-stream`). Prefer SSE over WebSockets for this cycle because SSE is simpler to implement on the FastAPI side, uses standard HTTP, and the `EventSource` browser API provides automatic reconnection with `Last-Event-Id`. Keep the event model bounded and compact — no artifact bodies over the wire. SSE is a notification mechanism; REST remains the source of truth.
- Event model: introduce a compact `MensuraEvent` envelope with `eventId` (UUID), `eventType` (string union), `occurredAt` (ISO 8601), optional `workspaceId`, `entityType`, `entityId`, `status`, and a minimal `summary` payload. Payloads are compact (status, summary text, no file contents or full artifact bodies). Supported event types: `run.status.changed`, `verification.created`, `application.created`, `undo.created`, `backup.created`. If one domain is not yet suitable for live updates, we defer it explicitly.
- Publisher model: inject a lightweight `EventPublisher` Protocol into services. Services call `publisher.publish(event)` after successful state changes. Event delivery is fire-and-forget — persistence/DB state remains the source of truth; SSE is a notification mechanism. No separate orchestration layer.
- SSE endpoint: `GET /api/v1/events/stream` returning `text/event-stream`. Supports optional `workspaceId` query parameter for filtering. Emits initial `connected` event on subscription open. Uses `Last-Event-Id` header for reconnect-friendly semantics via an in-memory sliding event buffer (last 100 events).
- Reliability: best-effort delivery. Studio must still recover via normal REST fetches on disconnect. Event replay is bounded to the buffer; no guaranteed durable replay. Disconnect is handled transparently via `EventSource` auto-reconnect.
- Studio integration: add a `useLiveEvents(workspaceId)` React hook wrapping `EventSource` + TanStack Query invalidation. When matching events arrive, invalidate the relevant query key to trigger a fresh REST fetch. Preserve existing polling as fallback — the `refetchInterval` on runs while `running` stays, but Studio now reacts to run status events without waiting for the next poll tick.
- Explicitly deferred: WebSockets, bidirectional events, per-entity subscription filtering beyond workspace, guaranteed durable event replay, events for Guard-only runs, change proposal approval/rejection events (covered by proposal status changes), background job orchestration, multi-instance event fanout, event persistence beyond in-memory buffer.
- Follow-up: shared event contracts → Core EventPublisher + SSE endpoint → hook into service transitions → Studio useLiveEvents hook → update artifact screens → tests → docs.

### 2026-07-20 — Implement and verify live SSE updates

- Files changed: `packages/shared-types/src/{events,events.test,index}.ts`; new Core `event_publisher.py`, `api/routers/events.py`; edited Core `service.py`, `verification_service.py`, `application_service.py`, `undo_service.py`, `backup_service.py`, `api/{router,dependencies}.py`, `main.py`, `pyproject.toml`, `tests/{test_openapi,test_sse}.py`; new Studio `features/events/useLiveEvents.ts`; edited Studio `app/App.tsx`; and `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- SSE strategy chosen: Server-Sent Events (`text/event-stream`) over standard HTTP via `sse-starlette`. Prefer SSE over WebSockets for this cycle — simpler FastAPI integration, automatic reconnection via browser `EventSource` API, and `Last-Event-Id` support for reconnect-friendly event replay.
- Event model chosen: compact `MensuraEvent` envelope (`eventId`, `eventType`, `occurredAt`, `workspaceId`, `entityType`, `entityId`, `status`, `summary`). Payloads are compact — status, summary text (≤200 chars), no file contents, artifact bodies, diffs, or patches. Supported event types: `run.status.changed`, `verification.created`, `application.created`, `undo.created`, `backup.created`.
- Core endpoint: `GET /api/v1/events/stream` with optional `workspaceId` query filter. Returns `text/event-stream` with `Cache-Control: no-cache`, `Connection: keep-alive`, `X-Accel-Buffering: no`. Emits initial `connected` event with buffer size on subscription.
- Publisher: `InMemoryEventPublisher` with a Protocol-based `EventPublisher` interface. Services receive optional `event_publisher` parameter (defaults to `None` for tests). Fire-and-forget publish via asyncio queues — no event delivery is the source of truth (DB/API remains authoritative). Sliding buffer of last 100 events supports `Last-Event-Id` replay.
- Services wired: `CoreService.execute_run()` publishes `run.status.changed` on both succeeded and failed transitions. `ProposalVerificationService._verify_in_sandbox()` publishes `verification.created`. `ChangeApplicationService._apply_to_live()` publishes `application.created`. `UndoService._execute_undo()` and `_refusal_artifact()` publish `undo.created`. `BackupService.create_backup()` publishes `backup.created`. All compact summaries (≤200 chars, no file bodies).
- Studio integration: `useLiveEvents({ workspaceId, queryClient })` hook creates an `EventSource` connection to Core's SSE endpoint, registers listeners for all five event types, and invalidates relevant TanStack Query keys on each event: `run.status.changed` → invalidate run query, `verification.created` → invalidate verification + workspace change-proposals, `application.created` → invalidate application + workspace applications, `undo.created` → invalidate undo + workspace undos, `backup.created` → invalidate backups list. Existing polling on runs (`refetchInterval: 1_000` while `running`) is preserved as fallback — events now trigger faster refresh without waiting for the next poll tick.
- Fallback behavior: REST remains the source of truth. On SSE disconnect, `EventSource` auto-reconnects (with `Last-Event-Id` replay when supported). Studio never replaces data with event payloads — it always refetches from REST. Any screen can be manually refreshed and will show correct state regardless of SSE status.
- Acceptance evidence: 124 Core tests pass (111 existing + 13 new SSE tests). New tests cover: publisher serialization and queue behavior, bounded summary truncation, buffer replay (empty after last-seen), buffer bounded at 100 events, verification/application/undo/backup event shapes with workspace IDs, connected event shape, subscribe/unsubscribe lifecycle, and publish-without-subscribers buffering. Core OpenAPI now covers 36 operations across 32 paths (up from 35/31 — new `/api/v1/events/stream`). Strict Studio TypeScript compilation passes with zero errors. Shared types compile with 47 tests (up from 42 — 5 new event contract tests). Existing run polling continues to work unchanged.
- What now works end-to-end: Studio subscribes to live SSE events on startup, receives `connected` confirmation, and auto-refreshes relevant queries when Core publishes status changes during run execution, sandbox verification, live application, undo, and backup creation. REST remains the fallback and source of truth for all data.
- Intentionally deferred: WebSockets, bidirectional events, per-entity subscription filtering beyond workspace ID, guaranteed durable event replay, events for Guard-only runs, change proposal approval/rejection events (covered by REST invalidations from mutations), background job orchestration, multi-instance event fanout, event persistence beyond in-memory buffer.
- Next best vertical slice: automate scheduled backups — add a configurable periodic backup timer (hourly/daily/weekly) with optional retention cap.

### 2026-07-21 — Start work cycle 19: durable background job execution

- Files changed: `docs/agent_memory.md`.
- Baseline: working tree carries the uncommitted cycles 15–18 (SQLite persistence, undo, backup, SSE) on clean commit `feaea03`. Re-read every synchronous execution path (`verification_service.verify`, `application_service.apply`, `undo_service.undo`, `backup_service.create_backup`), the SSE `event_publisher`/`events` router, the full `main.py` dependency wiring, the persistence layer (`database.py`, `models.py`, the SQL repo + migration patterns), the API problem registry/handlers, `conftest.py`, `test_openapi.py`, and the Studio client/query/`useLiveEvents`/App seams. No job or queue code exists yet; the four long-running operations currently run inline within their HTTP request.
- Queue strategy chosen: a SQLite-backed durable job queue integrated into the existing Core persistence (new `jobs` table + Alembic migration `004`). No Redis/Celery/RabbitMQ/external broker. A `Job` domain artifact carries `id`, `jobType`, `targetEntityType`, `targetEntityId` (nullable for backup), optional `workspaceId`, `status` (`queued | running | succeeded | failed`), `attemptCount`, a bounded typed `payload` (proposalId/verificationId/applicationId/label reference data only — never artifact bodies), `resultEntityType`/`resultEntityId` (the created artifact), a bounded `lastError` summary, and `createdAt`/`startedAt`/`finishedAt`.
- Job types (four): `proposal_verification` (target = change proposal), `application_apply` (target = change proposal, payload also carries verificationId), `application_undo` (target = application), `backup_create` (target = database, no target id). Restore stays explicit/synchronous and is deferred — it disposes the engine and requires a restart, which is unsafe to background.
- API compatibility decision: keep ALL existing synchronous endpoints (`POST …/verify`, `…/apply`, `…/undo`, `POST /backups`) unchanged so current REST artifacts, tests, and Studio flows keep their exact `201`+artifact semantics. Durable async is purely ADDITIVE via three new endpoints: `POST /api/v1/jobs` (enqueue → `201` + queued Job + Location), `GET /api/v1/jobs` (list, optional `workspaceId`/`status` filters), `GET /api/v1/jobs/{job_id}`. Enqueue does a light existence check on the target (reusing `ChangeProposalNotFoundError`/`ApplicationNotFoundError`, resolving `workspaceId` in the same lookup) and lets full eligibility/safety run at execution time.
- Worker model: a single in-process `JobWorker` started from a FastAPI `lifespan` (gated on `enable_worker=True`; production `create_sql_app()` enables it, tests leave it off and drive `process_next_job()` deterministically). The loop offloads blocking work via `asyncio.to_thread` and polls with a short interval (no cross-thread asyncio wake signal — polling is robust). Claiming is an atomic compare-and-set (`UPDATE … SET status='running' WHERE id=? AND status='queued'`, rowcount==1) so only one worker ever claims a job; SQLite serializes writes, and the existing per-workspace reservation locks in the verify/apply services still mutually exclude a worker job and an HTTP request on the same workspace.
- Job-vs-artifact boundary: a job is pure orchestration. Job SUCCESS = "the operation ran to completion and produced its artifact"; the artifact's own status still records the domain outcome (a `guard_failed` verification or `applied_guard_failed` application ⇒ job `succeeded`, artifact status unchanged). Only pre-write refusals that raise a `CoreError` (drift, unsafe path, not-approved, already-applied, ineligible undo, etc.) mark the job `failed` with a bounded `lastError`. The artifact chain (context pack → run → proposal → verification → application → undo, plus backup) is untouched; jobs reference artifacts, never replace them.
- Restart recovery strategy chosen: queued jobs persist in SQLite and are simply picked up by the worker after restart (no action needed). Interrupted `running` jobs are the risk; at startup, before the worker processes anything, they are atomically transitioned `running → failed` with a bounded "Interrupted by a Core restart; the operation's outcome is unknown — inspect the target artifact and re-enqueue if needed." This is the SAFE choice over auto-requeue: it never produces duplicate backups/verification artifacts, never silently re-applies, and is honest about unknown outcomes (the target artifact, if the op completed before the crash, is still present and inspectable).
- Retry decision: `attemptCount` is persisted (incremented on each claim) for forward-compatibility, but automatic retries are explicitly deferred this cycle — a failed job stays failed until a human re-enqueues.
- SSE integration: publish a compact `job.status.changed` event (bounded summary, no bodies) on enqueue (queued), claim (running), and terminal (succeeded/failed) through the existing `InMemoryEventPublisher`. Studio's `useLiveEvents` gains a `job.status.changed` handler that invalidates the jobs list + specific job query; the existing artifact invalidations still fire because the services publish their own `verification.created`/`application.created`/`undo.created`/`backup.created` events on success.
- Studio: a minimal `JobsPanel` lists jobs with status/type/target/timestamps/lastError, refreshes live via SSE, and offers one demonstrable enqueue action (queue a database backup job) to exercise the async path end-to-end in the UI.
- Safety rules preserved: queuing changes no digest check, guard requirement, path-safety boundary, single-apply/single-undo guard, or repository boundary — the worker calls the exact same service methods as the synchronous endpoints. No new provider or Git capability is introduced.
- Explicitly deferred: automatic retries, job cancellation, priorities, scheduled/cron jobs, restore-as-job, distributed/multi-node coordination, and changing the existing synchronous endpoints to enqueue.
- Follow-up: shared Job contracts → Core models/repo/service/worker → SQL persistence + migration → job API + problems → main.py lifespan wiring → tests → Studio Jobs view → docs → live restart verification.

### 2026-07-21 — Complete work cycle 19: durable background job execution

Cycle 19 added a SQLite-backed durable job queue so the four long-running operations (proposal verification, application apply, application undo, backup creation) can each run as persisted background jobs instead of only inline in the HTTP request. [Full cycle 19 details retained above.]

### 2026-07-21 — Start work cycle 20: job-first Studio flows + explicit single-retry

Goal: Make durable jobs the primary Studio path for proposal verification, application apply, and application undo, and add a bounded explicit single-retry path for failed jobs.

Product scope:
- Studio launches verify/apply/undo through the durable job path (with direct buttons kept as secondary)
- job-aware UI on proposal/application panels (inline status, result linkage, error display)
- explicit single-retry for eligible failed jobs via `POST /api/v1/jobs/{job_id}/retry`
- clear linkage between jobs and resulting artifacts
- minimal Core additions: retry eligibility, retry API, new retry tracking fields

Retry strategy:
- Only failed jobs are retry-eligible
- Only one retry per original job (original marked `retryEligible=False` after spawn)
- Retry creates a new linked child `Job`, never mutates history
- Retry child is itself retry-eligible once (chain: original → retry1 → retry2 max)
- No automatic retry scheduling — all retries are explicit user actions
- Domain safety validations run identically during retried execution (Guard, digest checks, drift detection)
- Unsupported job types (backup_create) are not retryable
- Four new fields on Job: `retryOfJobId`, `rootJobId`, `retryEligible`, `retryCount`
