**What now works end-to-end:**
- From the **verification panel**: user clicks "Verify as background job", a `proposal_verification` job is enqueued, worker executes it, result verification artifact appears in the verification list (polled + cached)
- From the **application panel**: user clicks "Apply as background job", an `application_apply` job runs, live tree is written, application artifact linked
- From the **undo section**: user clicks "Undo as background job", an `application_undo` job runs, live tree is restored
- From the **Jobs panel**: failed eligible jobs show "Retry (single attempt remaining)" button; clicking enqueues a new linked child job; exhausted jobs show "No retries remaining"; retry lineage is displayed
- **SSE**: `job.status.changed` events published for both original (exhaustion) and retry (creation) — existing `useLiveEvents` hook invalidates job queries automatically

**What was intentionally deferred:**
- Job cancellation, priorities, scheduling, automatic retries
- Restore-as-job (restore stays synchronous)
- Multi-node workers
- EntityJobBadge component (inline per-entity job status) — scope reduced to keep feature minimal
- Fixing pre-existing React 19 / @testing-library/react `React.act is not a function` compatibility issue

**Cleanup completed:**
- Updated `docs/agent_memory.md` with cycle 20 start/completion
- Fixed `test_openapi.py` path assertion
- Root README "process memory" wording note left for next cycle (minimal scope)

- Files changed (new): `packages/shared-types/src/{jobs,jobs.test}.ts`; Core `job_models.py`, `job_repositories.py`, `job_service.py`, `job_worker.py`, `persistence/repositories/job.py`, `api/routers/jobs.py`, `migrations/versions/004_jobs.py`, `tests/{test_jobs,test_jobs_api}.py`; Studio `features/jobs/{JobsPanel,JobsPanel.test}.tsx`.
- Files changed (edited): `packages/shared-types/src/{events,index}.ts`; Core `exceptions.py`, `api/{problems,dependencies,router}.py`, `main.py`, `persistence/{models,__init__}.py`, `tests/{conftest,test_openapi,test_persistence}.py`; Studio `api/coreClient.ts`, `app/{queryClient,App}.tsx`, `features/events/useLiveEvents.ts`, `styles.css`, `test/render.tsx`; root/Core/Studio READMEs; `docs/agent_memory.md`. No dependency or lockfile changed (SQLite/SQLAlchemy/Alembic/sse-starlette were already present).
- Job queue strategy chosen: a durable SQLite-backed queue integrated into the existing Core persistence — a new `jobs` table (Alembic migration `004`, clean up/down) holding `Job` schema-v1 rows with `jobType`, `targetEntityType`/`targetEntityId` (nullable for backup), nullable `workspaceId` (plain indexed column, not an FK, since jobs are loosely-coupled orchestration and `targetEntityId` is polymorphic), `status` (`queued | running | succeeded | failed`, indexed), `attemptCount`, a bounded typed `payload` (proposalId/verificationId/applicationId/label only — no artifact bodies), `resultEntityType`/`resultEntityId`, a bounded `lastError`, and `createdAt`/`startedAt`/`finishedAt`. No Redis/Celery/RabbitMQ/broker.
- API shape (additive, zero breaking changes): `POST /api/v1/jobs` (discriminated-union body on `jobType`; `201` + queued `Job` + `Location`), `GET /api/v1/jobs?workspaceId=&status=&jobType=`, `GET /api/v1/jobs/{job_id}`. New problem `job-not-found` (404); enqueue reuses `change-proposal-not-found`/`application-not-found` for missing targets. Core OpenAPI is now 42 operations across 37 paths (up from 39/35 — added POST/GET `/api/v1/jobs` and GET `/api/v1/jobs/{job_id}`). The existing synchronous `…/verify`, `…/apply`, `…/undo`, and `POST /backups` endpoints are unchanged and keep their exact `201`+artifact semantics — durable async is opt-in via the job API.
- Worker model: a single in-process `JobWorker` wired for every app but auto-started only from the FastAPI `lifespan` when `enable_worker=True` (production `create_sql_app` enables it; tests leave it off and drive `process_next_job()` deterministically). `run_forever` offloads each blocking `process_next_job` via `asyncio.to_thread` and polls at a 0.5 s idle interval (no cross-thread asyncio wake — polling is robust and also picks up restart-recovered jobs). Claiming is an atomic compare-and-set (`UPDATE jobs SET status='running',started_at=?,attempt_count=attempt_count+1 WHERE id=? AND status='queued'`, rowcount==1); SQLite serializes writes so only one worker ever claims a job. `mark_succeeded`/`mark_failed` are short compare-and-set transactions guarded on `status='running'`. The pre-existing per-workspace reservation locks in the verify/apply services still mutually exclude a worker job and an HTTP request on the same workspace.
- Worker recovery strategy chosen: queued jobs persist and are simply drained by the worker after restart. Interrupted `running` jobs are recovered at startup (before the worker processes anything) by an atomic `running → failed` transition carrying an honest "Interrupted by a Core restart; the operation's outcome is unknown — inspect the target artifact and re-enqueue if needed" summary. This is the SAFE choice over auto-requeue: it never produces duplicate backups/verification artifacts, never silently re-applies, and is truthful about unknown outcomes. Automatic retries are deferred (`attemptCount` is persisted for forward-compatibility); restore stays explicit/synchronous and is never queued.
- Job-vs-artifact boundary (preserved safety): the worker calls the exact same service method the synchronous endpoint calls, so every digest check, Guard requirement, path-safety boundary, and single-apply/single-undo guard is intact, and no new provider or Git capability is introduced. Job `succeeded` = "the operation ran to completion and produced its artifact"; the artifact's own status still records the domain outcome (a `guard_failed` verification or `applied_guard_failed` application still yields a `succeeded` job). Only pre-write refusals that raise a `CoreError` (drift, unsafe path, not-approved, already-applied, ineligible undo, …) mark the job `failed` with a bounded, non-leaking summary; unexpected exceptions become a generic failure without leaking internals. The artifact chain (context pack → run → proposal → verification → application → undo, plus backup) is untouched.
- SSE integration: a compact `job.status.changed` event (bounded summary, no bodies) is published through the existing `InMemoryEventPublisher` on enqueue (queued), claim (running), and terminal (succeeded/failed). Studio's `useLiveEvents` gains a handler that invalidates the jobs list + specific job query; the services still publish their own `verification.created`/`application.created`/`undo.created`/`backup.created` events on success, so artifact screens refresh too.
- Studio: a minimal `JobsPanel` lists jobs with status badge, type label, target, timestamps, produced-artifact reference, and last-error summary, refreshed live over SSE (10 s poll fallback), plus a demonstrable "queue backup job" action. Also fixed a pre-existing cycle-18 defect: `useLiveEvents` now guards `typeof EventSource === "undefined"`, so `App.test.tsx` (which crashed in jsdom with "EventSource is not defined") passes and the hook is a safe no-op in non-browser environments.
- What now works end-to-end: proposal verification, application apply, application undo, and backup creation can each be enqueued as a durable job over `POST /api/v1/jobs`; a single in-process worker atomically claims and executes them, persisting `queued → running → succeeded|failed` with timestamps and (on success) the produced artifact's id; Studio observes the whole lifecycle live via REST + SSE. Job state survives a Core restart, queued jobs are drained after restart, and a job interrupted mid-run is recovered to `failed` with an honest summary. All existing safety guarantees and synchronous endpoints are intact.
- Automated verification: 153 Core tests pass (124 prior + 29 new — 19 in `test_jobs.py` covering enqueue, worker claim/dispatch/execution, SSE event ordering, refusal + unexpected-error propagation, claim atomicity/compare-and-set and recovery across InMemory **and** SQLite repos, and SQL persist-across-restart; 10 in `test_jobs_api.py` covering HTTP enqueue/list/filter/get, 404/422, and real worker execution of verification/apply/undo jobs plus a drift-refused apply job and a SQL backup job end-to-end). Ruff lint/format clean on all new/edited files. Root `pnpm check` passes: recursive strict TypeScript, 57 shared-type tests (10 new job contract tests), 69 Studio tests across 18 files (4 new JobsPanel tests, App.test.tsx fixed), both production builds, and `cargo check`.
- Live acceptance (process restart during queued/running work): a scripted run enqueued three backup jobs into a temp SQLite DB and claimed one (`alpha`) to running, then killed the process; a real Uvicorn `create_sql_app` restarted on the same DB with the worker enabled. On startup it recovered `alpha` to `failed` with the exact restart summary (attemptCount 1), and drained the two queued jobs (`beta`, `gamma`) to `succeeded`, each producing a real backup artifact — 2 backups created after restart. Temp DB/WAL/SHM and backup dir were cleaned up.
- Intentionally deferred: automatic job retries, job cancellation, priorities, scheduled/cron jobs, restore-as-job, external brokers / distributed multi-node coordination, and changing the existing synchronous endpoints to enqueue. Pre-existing doc debt in the root README's opening paragraph (still says "process memory", predating cycle-15 SQLite persistence) and Ruff-format drift in a few untouched cycle-16/17/18 files were left as-is to keep this cycle's diff focused.
- Next best vertical slice: a job detail/enqueue surface in Studio that lets a user launch verify/apply/undo as durable jobs directly from the proposal/application panels (not just backup), plus optional bounded, explicit single-retry of a failed job (turning the already-persisted `attemptCount` into a real retry path) — the natural next step now that the durable queue and worker exist.

- Which pagination and authentication contracts should extend the implemented Core v1 resource/error schemas?
- Local MVP persistence uses SQLite with SQLAlchemy 2.0 + Alembic; Postgres migration is deferred but the architecture stays open via `MENSURA_DATABASE_URL`.
- Should a second provider be added before durable run history, and what cross-platform credential-backend acceptance matrix is required beyond the verified macOS Keychain path?
- What exact sandbox guarantees are required for local command execution on macOS, Linux, and Windows?
- Which project-specific ignore mechanism should extend the fixed Vault rules before team-scale indexing, and when should hashing/durable branch-aware snapshots become necessary?
- How are plugin signatures rooted and verified, and which permissions are allowed for the first local plugin loader?
- Are the `[cite:…]` markers in the specifications backed by a source bibliography that should be added to the repository?

### 2026-07-21 — Start cycle 21: audit & hardening (verification-first, no new product scope)

- Intent: a full end-to-end engineering audit of the committed system (through cycle 20, commit `367f3a9`), fixing only clearly-critical or low-risk/high-value issues, then a prioritized report. Not a feature cycle.
- Baseline established: Core `165 passed` (pytest). Shared-types green. **Studio `5 failed | 64 passed`** — the committed `main` has a red Studio suite. gitignore clean (no tracked venv/node_modules/pnpm-store/pyc). No secret logging found (grep of api_key/password/token in log/print sites is empty). OpenAPI test enforces camelCase + `application/problem+json` + forbidden-field discipline (no patch/content/repositoryPath/command). `providers.json` temp-suffix works (no `with_suffix` bug).
- Architecture verified coherent: artifact lineage context pack → run → proposal → verification → application → undo, plus backup + jobs. Persistence schema is high quality (FKs indexed; correct unique constraints on workspace root, guard-run/vault-snapshot per workspace, proposal per run, application per proposal, undo per application; JSON for bounded payloads; clean Pydantic round-trips). Problem-details layer is exhaustive and RFC 9457-consistent. Writers (apply/undo) are two-phase digest-checked atomic replaces with symlink/`..`/absolute refusal via `safe_paths.resolve_safe_target`. Guard runner is shell-free argv, process-group isolated, bounded output, env-allowlisted. Provider boundary passes only persisted task+manifest (no root/fs/git). Keyring for secrets, `0600` config file.
- Findings to FIX this cycle (critical or low-risk/high-value):
  1. **Docs point users at the non-durable in-memory app.** `main:app` (module-level) is InMemory; the durable app is `create_sql_app` (used only by the `mensura-core` script / `run()`). Both READMEs tell users `uvicorn mensura_core.main:app`, which silently defeats the entire SQLite-persistence story. → fix run commands.
  2. **Studio suite red on `main`.** 5 stale-label assertions in `ProposalVerificationSection.test.tsx` / `ProposalApplicationSection.test.tsx` still expect pre-cycle-20 button names ("Verify in isolated sandbox", "Apply to live working tree") after the job-first rename to "Verify (direct)" / "Apply (direct)". → align assertions with shipped UI.
  3. **Cross-thread `asyncio.Queue` publish.** `event_publisher.publish()` is called from the worker thread (`asyncio.to_thread`) and from sync HTTP endpoints (FastAPI threadpool), doing `queue.put_nowait()` on `asyncio.Queue` — not thread-safe (schedules `loop.call_soon` from the wrong thread). → make publish thread-safe via captured loop + `call_soon_threadsafe`; preserves best-effort semantics.
  4. **`backup_service.create_backup` leaks a pooled connection.** `self._engine.raw_connection().driver_connection` never closes the connection proxy. → wrap in try/finally close.
  5. **Core README drift:** claims "undo execution is not implemented", "Background workers, brokers, streaming/SSE, retries… remain deferred", and "in-memory" storage — all false since cycles 15–20. Root README opening still says "process memory". → correct.
- Findings to DOCUMENT (Schedule/Defer — not fixing to avoid speculative churn): cross-service workspace locking (apply vs undo use separate in-process locks; concurrent live writes possible but digest-guarded); verification-sandbox temp-worktree leak on crash (no startup sweep); no explicit SQLite `busy_timeout` PRAGMA (relies on 5s driver default); Guard forces `PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD` on the user's own pytest; `database.create_persistence_engine` runs `mkdir` unconditionally for non-sqlite URLs; API integration tests all use InMemory repos (SQL path + worker lifespan + migrations not exercised through the HTTP app); unbounded backup/artifact/job/event retention; single-process in-memory SSE buffer (no durable replay).

### 2026-07-21 — Complete cycle 21: audit & hardening

- Files changed (10 + this journal): `README.md`, `apps/studio/README.md`, `services/core/README.md` (doc drift), `docs/mensura_architecture_overview.md` (stripped 28 `[web:NNN]` citation-noise markers), `services/core/src/mensura_core/event_publisher.py` (thread-safe publish), `services/core/src/mensura_core/backup_service.py` (raw_connection leak), `services/core/src/mensura_core/api/routers/events.py` (async-generator return type), `apps/studio/src/features/change-proposals/ProposalApplicationSection.tsx` (real bug), the two proposal test files, and `services/core/tests/test_undo_api.py` (pre-existing E501). No dependency/lockfile/schema/migration change.
- Fixed this cycle:
  1. **Docs pointed at the non-durable in-memory app** — root/Core/Studio READMEs now run `mensura_core.main:create_sql_app --factory` and explain that bare `:app` is the ephemeral in-memory variant. Verified `create_sql_app` boots (migrations 001→005), starts the worker, and runs a backup job to completion against a temp DB via TestClient.
  2. **Studio suite was red on `main` (5 failing)** — 4 were stale button-label assertions (job-first rename); the 5th uncovered a **real bug**: `apply.error` rendered twice (section-level `ProblemDetailsView` at the old line 245 duplicated the one inside `ApplyGate`). Removed the redundant render. Studio now 69/69 green, typecheck clean.
  3. **Cross-thread `asyncio.Queue` publish** — `InMemoryEventPublisher` now captures each subscriber's loop at `subscribe()` and delivers via `loop.call_soon_threadsafe` under a `threading.Lock`; buffer append stays GIL-atomic. Verified by publishing from a separate thread into a loop subscriber (previously undefined behavior). Existing 13 SSE tests still pass.
  4. **`backup_service.create_backup` pooled-connection leak** — `raw_connection()` is now closed in a `finally`. Exercised by the end-to-end backup-job run.
  5. **Doc drift corrected** — Core README no longer claims undo is unimplemented / SSE+workers+retries deferred / "in-memory" storage / "process-local" packs; root README no longer references an "in-memory limitation".
  6. Minor: `events._stream_events` typed `AsyncIterator[dict[str,str]]`; 2 pre-existing E501 in `test_undo_api.py` wrapped.
- Verification: Core `165 passed`, `ruff check src tests` clean, my new code `ruff format`-clean; shared-types `60 passed`; Studio `69 passed` + `tsc --noEmit` clean; live durable-app + worker + backup-job smoke test passed.
- Deliberately NOT bundled (documented for a dedicated pass): repo-wide `ruff format` drift (14 files, incl. pre-existing regions of events.py/backup_service.py — `ruff check` already passes and Guard uses `check`, not `format`); the Schedule/Defer findings listed in the start entry.
- Triage of remaining findings:
  - **Schedule next:** unify per-workspace locking across apply/undo/verify (single reservation registry) so concurrent live-tree writers can't interleave; add an API-level integration test suite that runs against the SQL app + worker lifespan + migrations (today only unit tests hit SQL); repo-wide `ruff format` pass; verification-sandbox startup sweep for orphaned `mensura-verification-*` worktrees; retention/pruning policy for backups + terminal jobs + old artifacts.
  - **Defer:** explicit SQLite `busy_timeout` PRAGMA; reconsider `PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD` for user pytest; guard `mkdir` behind `startswith('sqlite')` in `create_persistence_engine`; durable/multi-instance SSE replay; pagination + auth contracts; second provider; plugin loader.
- Biggest residual risks: (a) concurrent apply-vs-undo on one workspace relies solely on digest guards (no shared lock) — safe today for single-user, must fix before any multi-actor use; (b) SQL persistence path is not covered by HTTP-level integration tests, only unit tests + one manual smoke; (c) unbounded local growth (backups/jobs/events) over long-term single-user use.
- Next recommended slice: **unified per-workspace write reservation** shared by verify/apply/undo (and the worker), replacing the three independent `_active_workspaces` locks with one registry — small, safety-focused, and closes the only concurrency gap where two live-tree writers could interleave. It naturally precedes the API-level SQL integration tests that would regression-guard it.

### 2026-07-21 — Start cycle 22: unified workspace write reservation + HTTP-level durable SQL integration tests

- Intent (hardening/concurrency, no product expansion): introduce ONE process-wide per-workspace reservation shared by every live working-tree writer, and add HTTP-level integration coverage for the durable SQL app path (real startup, migrations, worker lifespan).
- Baseline re-verified in code at commit `93e5366` (clean tree). The current write-coordination is fragmented:
  - `ChangeApplicationService` (apply): own `_active_workspaces: set[UUID]` + `_active_lock: threading.Lock`, `_reserve`/`_release` in a try/finally, raises `ApplicationInProgressError` → 409 `application-in-progress`. **Writes the live working tree.**
  - `UndoService` (undo): **NO reservation at all** — writes the live working tree guarded only by digest checks. This is the critical gap: apply and undo can interleave on one workspace.
  - `ProposalVerificationService` (verify): own separate `_active_workspaces` + `_active_lock`, raises `ProposalVerificationInProgressError` → 409 `verification-in-progress`. Materializes its sandbox from **committed HEAD** via `git worktree add --detach HEAD` (verified in `verification_sandbox.py`) and writes ONLY inside a temp worktree — never the live tree.
  - `GuardService` (standalone guard): own guard-run reservation; runs configured ruff/pytest against the live tree (reads it).
  - `JobWorker._dispatch` calls the exact same `application_service.apply` / `undo_service.undo` methods, so whatever the services acquire, the worker inherits; `process_next_job` already catches `CoreError` → `mark_failed`, so a reservation refusal maps to an honest failed job with a bounded `lastError`, before any artifact is written.
- Design decided:
  1. New `workspace_reservation.py`: `WorkspaceWriteReservation` — a single registry keyed by `workspace_id`, backed by one `threading.Lock` + a `dict[UUID, WorkspaceWriteHolder]`. `reserve(workspace_id, *, holder_kind, target_entity_type, target_entity_id)` is a context manager that atomically refuses (never queues) a second claim with `WorkspaceWriteInProgressError`, and releases in `finally`. `WorkspaceWriteHolder` carries diagnostics (`holder_kind`, `target_entity_type`, `target_entity_id`, `acquired_at`). Exposed on `app.state.workspace_write_reservation`.
  2. **apply and undo** both acquire the SAME injected reservation (holder kinds `application_apply` / `application_undo`). The worker is covered transitively (no bypass).
  3. **verification does NOT acquire it** — intentional. Rationale: its sandbox is a worktree of the committed HEAD, apply/undo never commit/move HEAD/touch `.git`, and verification never writes the live tree, so its input is stable under concurrent live-tree writes. It keeps its own verification-level serialization. Taking the live-tree reservation would wrongly block apply/undo during a slow sandbox pytest run.
  4. **backup does NOT acquire it** (operates on the SQLite DB file, not the workspace tree). **standalone guard does NOT** (reads the tree, keeps its own reservation; a read/write lock is out of scope for a *write* reservation and would force apply/undo's internal guard sub-runs to be reentrant). The internal guard sub-run inside apply/undo already runs under the held write reservation via `execute_guard_checks(...)` (a plain function, not `GuardService`), so post-write guard sees a stable tree with no self-conflict.
  5. Error contract: `WorkspaceWriteInProgressError(CoreError)` → new `urn:mensura:problem:workspace-write-in-progress` (409 Conflict / busy). Retire `ApplicationInProgressError` + `application-in-progress`. Both apply (`APPLICATION_CONFLICT_RESPONSE`) and undo (`UNDO_CONFLICT_RESPONSE`) endpoints already document a generic 409, so no router/OpenAPI path change is required.
  6. Optional hardening (in scope, low-risk): add `PRAGMA busy_timeout = 5000` to `_configure_sqlite_pragmas` so the durable SQL path has an explicit, driver-independent 5s busy wait.
- HTTP-level durable SQL integration tests (new `test_durable_sql_app.py`): boot the real durable configuration (`create_app(run_migrations_on_startup=True, use_sql=True, enable_worker=True, ...)` against a temp DB/backup dir — the `create_sql_app` shape) and cover: app startup + `/health`; migrations produced the expected schema (`alembic_version` at head, `jobs`/`backups` tables present); worker lifespan starts and drains a real backup job to `succeeded` (polling the HTTP job endpoint, not `process_next_job()` by hand); a contention scenario (hold the exposed reservation, then an apply/undo endpoint returns 409 `workspace-write-in-progress`); a structured problem response (unknown job → 404 `job-not-found` in `application/problem+json`); and a backup endpoint smoke path. Only the provider and guard-command-runner are injected fakes (real LLM/guard aren't hermetic); persistence, migrations, worker, reservation, and routing are all real.
- Follow-up order: reservation module + unit tests → wire apply/undo + main.py + expose on app.state → retire ApplicationInProgressError, add the unified problem → busy_timeout → HTTP-level SQL integration tests → docs (README, Core README) → full verification (pytest + ruff) → live two-competing-operations check.

### 2026-07-21 — Complete cycle 22: unified workspace write reservation + HTTP-level durable SQL integration tests

- Files changed (3 new, 9 edited; no dependency/lockfile/migration/schema change):
  - **New:** `services/core/src/mensura_core/workspace_reservation.py` (the registry), `services/core/tests/test_workspace_reservation.py` (8 unit tests), `services/core/tests/test_durable_sql_app.py` (8 HTTP-level durable-SQL integration tests).
  - **Edited (src):** `exceptions.py` (added `WorkspaceWriteInProgressError`, removed `ApplicationInProgressError`), `application_service.py` (inject `write_reservation`, replace internal `_active_workspaces`/`_active_lock`/`_reserve`/`_release` with `with self._write_reservation.reserve(...)`), `undo_service.py` (inject `write_reservation`, wrap `_execute_undo` in the reservation — undo had NONE before), `main.py` (create one `WorkspaceWriteReservation`, expose on `app.state.workspace_write_reservation`, inject the same instance into apply + undo), `api/problems.py` (swap import/type/handler → `WORKSPACE_WRITE_IN_PROGRESS_TYPE`), `persistence/database.py` (`PRAGMA busy_timeout = 5000`).
  - **Edited (tests/docs):** `tests/test_jobs_api.py` (new worker-reservation-refusal test), `README.md`, `services/core/README.md`, `apps/studio/README.md`, this journal.
- **Reservation strategy chosen:** one process-wide `WorkspaceWriteReservation` — a single `threading.Lock` guarding a `dict[workspace_id → WorkspaceWriteHolder]`. `reserve(workspace_id, *, holder_kind, target_entity_type, target_entity_id)` is a context manager: atomically refuses a second claim (raising immediately — **never queues**), releases in `finally`, and only releases its own holder (defensive against double-exit). `WorkspaceWriteHolder` carries diagnostics (`holder_kind`, `target_entity_type`, `target_entity_id`, `acquired_at`); `is_reserved()`/`active_holders()` expose state for tests. Single-process, local-first, no broker/distributed lock. Replaced the two independent `_active_workspaces` locks (apply had its own; undo had none) with this one shared object injected by `main.py`.
- **Which operations acquire it:** **apply** (`holder_kind="application_apply"`, target = proposal) and **undo** (`holder_kind="application_undo"`, target = application) — the only two live-working-tree writers. The **job worker** is covered transitively with no bypass: `_dispatch` calls the same `apply`/`undo` service methods, and `process_next_job` already catches `CoreError` → `mark_failed`, so a reservation refusal becomes an honest `failed` job with a bounded `lastError` and no partial artifact (the reservation is claimed before any write or artifact persistence).
- **Does verification acquire it? NO — intentional.** Verification materializes its sandbox from the committed `HEAD` (`git worktree add --detach HEAD`) and writes only inside a temp worktree; apply/undo never commit, move `HEAD`, or touch `.git`, so verification's input is stable under concurrent live-tree writes and it never writes the live tree. It keeps its own per-workspace verification serialization (`ProposalVerificationInProgressError`). Taking the live-tree reservation would incorrectly block apply/undo during a slow sandbox pytest run for an operation that provably doesn't touch the live tree. **backup** does not acquire it (snapshots the SQLite DB, not the tree). **standalone guard** does not (reads the tree, keeps its own guard-run reservation; a read/write lock is out of scope for a *write* reservation and would force apply/undo's internal `execute_guard_checks(...)` sub-run to be reentrant). The internal guard sub-run inside apply/undo already runs under the held write reservation, so post-write guard sees a stable tree.
- **Error contract:** `WorkspaceWriteInProgressError(CoreError)` → `urn:mensura:problem:workspace-write-in-progress`, **409 Conflict** (treated as busy/conflict, not auto-retried), consistent across sync HTTP (apply/undo endpoints) and job-driven (`lastError`) paths. Retired `ApplicationInProgressError` + `application-in-progress`. No OpenAPI path/operation change — both apply (`APPLICATION_CONFLICT_RESPONSE`) and undo (`UNDO_CONFLICT_RESPONSE`) already documented a generic 409; still 42 operations / 37 paths.
- **Integration tests added:** `test_durable_sql_app.py` boots the real durable config (`run_migrations_on_startup=True, use_sql=True, enable_worker=True`, temp DB + backup dir; only the provider and guard-runner are injected fakes) and covers — app startup + `/health`; migrations at Alembic head with `workspaces/applications/undos/backups/jobs` tables present (asserted via a direct sqlite3 read of `alembic_version`); **real worker lifespan** draining an enqueued backup job to `succeeded` by polling the HTTP job endpoint (genuinely exercises the background loop + `asyncio.to_thread`, unlike the pre-existing `process_next_job()`-driven tests); apply refused while the reservation is held (409 `workspace-write-in-progress`, nothing written, no artifact); undo refused while an apply-kind reservation is held (proves the two writers can't interleave); the shared-instance wiring (`change_application_service._write_reservation is undo_service._write_reservation is app.state.workspace_write_reservation`); unknown job → 404 `job-not-found` in `application/problem+json`; and a backup create/list/get smoke path. Plus `test_jobs_api.py::test_apply_job_fails_honestly_when_the_workspace_reservation_is_held` (worker path → failed job, no partial artifact) and 8 reservation unit tests including a cross-thread mutual-exclusion test.
- **busy_timeout:** ADDED — `PRAGMA busy_timeout = 5000` in `_configure_sqlite_pragmas` (const `SQLITE_BUSY_TIMEOUT_MS = 5000`), alongside WAL + `foreign_keys`. Rationale: with WAL, SQLite still serializes writers, and the single worker can briefly contend with a synchronous request; setting it at the SQLite level is explicit and driver-independent (was previously only the pysqlite ~5s default).
- **What now works end-to-end:** apply and undo on one workspace are mutually exclusive within the process regardless of origin (sync request or background job); a competing live-tree writer is refused immediately with a clear, consistent structured 409 (or an honest failed job) and writes nothing. **Live verification:** a scripted race of 5 concurrent `POST …/undo` calls on the same application against the real durable SQL app (migrations + worker + reservation) produced exactly 1 success (201), 4 refusals all `urn:mensura:problem:workspace-write-in-progress` (409), exactly 1 persisted undo artifact, and the deleted file restored exactly once. All prior safety guarantees (digest checks, Guard, path safety, single-apply/single-undo, artifact lineage) are intact.
- **Verification:** Core `182 passed` (165 prior + 17 new: 8 reservation unit, 8 durable-SQL integration, 1 job reservation-refusal). `ruff check src tests` clean; all new/edited-by-me code is `ruff format`-clean (remaining format drift is pre-existing in untouched regions of `exceptions.py`/`undo_service.py`, consistent with the cycle-21 note; Guard uses `check`, not `format`). Live 5-way race: PASS. Shared-types/Studio untouched (no TS change this cycle).
- **Intentionally deferred:** verification/backup/standalone-guard joining the reservation (documented non-participants); a read/write (shared-read + exclusive-write) lock so standalone guard excludes concurrent apply/undo; blocking/queued reservation acquisition with fairness (current contract is refuse-immediately); cross-process/distributed coordination; verification-sandbox startup sweep for orphaned `mensura-verification-*` worktrees; retention/pruning for backups + terminal jobs + old artifacts; the repo-wide `ruff format` pass.
- **Next best slice:** verification-sandbox startup sweep + a retention/pruning policy for unbounded local growth (backups, terminal jobs, artifacts) — the two remaining hardening items from the cycle-21 triage now that the concurrency gap and the SQL-path integration-test gap are both closed. A read/write lock making standalone guard exclude live-tree writers is a smaller optional follow-up if guard-vs-apply result consistency ever matters.

### 2026-07-21 — Start cycle 23: verification-sandbox startup sweep + minimal retention/pruning

- Intent (hardening/operability, no product expansion): stop leaving orphaned `mensura-verification-*` worktrees/temp dirs behind after a crash, and bound the two unbounded operational byproducts (backups + terminal jobs) with a conservative, explicit retention policy. Do not weaken any existing safety guarantee or artifact semantics; keep it local-first, single-process, no external scheduler/cron.
- Baseline re-verified in code at commit `93e5366` + uncommitted cycle-22 tree (clean, `182 passed`). Re-read the sandbox lifecycle (`verification_sandbox.py`: `GitWorktreeSandboxFactory` → `tempfile.mkdtemp(prefix="mensura-verification-")` then `git worktree add --detach <dir>/worktree HEAD`; cleanup does `git worktree remove --force` + `shutil.rmtree(temp_dir)` + `git worktree prune`), the backup service/repo/model (global DB snapshots, no workspace, no retention cap, filename `backup-{ts}-{uuid8}.db` under `MENSURA_BACKUP_DIR`), the job service/repo/model (terminal = succeeded|failed; retry lineage via plain non-FK `retry_of_job_id`/`root_job_id`), the durable `create_app`/`create_sql_app` lifespan wiring, and the cycle-22 `test_durable_sql_app.py` integration harness. Confirmed backup tests create ≤1 backup and job tests ≤2 jobs, so conservative defaults won't disturb them.
- **Part A — sandbox sweep design.** Single-process is the key safety lever: the sweep runs once in the lifespan *before* the worker starts and before traffic, so no verification can be in flight — any matching sandbox at startup is necessarily orphaned from a previous process. Rules: (1) deterministic ownership — only consider dirs whose name starts with `mensura-verification-`; (2) structure check — only delete a candidate whose layout matches what the factory creates (empty, or exactly one child named `worktree`), never an arbitrary path; a mismatch is skipped + warned, not deleted; (3) rely on Git's own `git worktree prune` per workspace for stale `.git/worktrees` metadata rather than hand-editing internals; (4) every failure is a logged warning, never a startup abort. To make the parent dir explicit + testable (and to let the durable integration test drive a controlled root through the real factory), add `MENSURA_SANDBOX_DIR` (default = system temp) that BOTH the factory (`dir=`) and the sweeper scan. Order: delete orphaned temp dirs first, then prune per-workspace metadata. Summary logged: inspected / removed / skipped / worktrees_pruned. Gated behind a new `sweep_verification_sandboxes` flag (default off; `create_sql_app` enables it) so the many unit-test app instances don't scan the real temp dir.
- **Part B — retention design.** Scope strictly to operational byproducts: **backups** and **terminal jobs**. Never prune core domain artifacts (tasks, proposals, verifications, applications, undos) or queued/running jobs. One reusable `RetentionPolicy` (pure, unit-tested): keep an item iff it is within `keep_at_least` newest OR within newest `max_count` OR newer than `max_age_days`; prune only when it fails all three (i.e. beyond the count AND older than the age). `0` in a dimension makes that dimension inactive; **both 0 = retention disabled** (the documented off-switch). Conservative defaults: backups `count=10`, `days=30`, `keep_at_least=1` (never delete the only/newest backup); terminal jobs `count=200`, `days=30`, `keep_at_least=0`. Env overrides: `MENSURA_BACKUP_RETENTION_COUNT/DAYS`, `MENSURA_JOB_RETENTION_COUNT/DAYS`. Safety: backup file unlink happens before the DB-row delete and a file-unlink failure skips the row delete (row⟹file stays consistent); job pruning skips any terminal job still referenced as a retry parent/root by a retained job (lineage integrity); all deletions are best-effort (warn, never crash). Cadence: prune at startup (backups + jobs) and again after each backup creation (backups only — the primary growth vector); job pruning is startup-only this cycle.
- Follow-up order: sandbox prefix/parent helper in `verification_sandbox.py` → `verification_sweep.py` + unit tests → wire sweep into lifespan + durable integration test → `retention.py` + policy unit tests → backup repo `delete` + `BackupService.prune` → job repo `delete` + `JobService.prune_jobs` → wire startup pruning + post-create backup prune → retention tests (incl. edge cases) → READMEs + this journal → full pytest + ruff → manual durable run (seed backups/jobs/orphan sandbox, restart, confirm).

### 2026-07-21 — Complete cycle 23: verification-sandbox startup sweep + minimal retention/pruning

- **Files changed (4 new, 11 edited; no dependency/lockfile/migration/schema change):**
  - **New (src):** `services/core/src/mensura_core/verification_sweep.py` (orphaned-sandbox sweep), `services/core/src/mensura_core/retention.py` (reusable `RetentionPolicy`).
  - **New (tests):** `services/core/tests/test_verification_sweep.py` (10), `services/core/tests/test_retention.py` (19).
  - **Edited (src):** `verification_sandbox.py` (deterministic `SANDBOX_TEMP_PREFIX`/`SANDBOX_WORKTREE_DIRNAME` constants + `sandbox_parent_dir()` honoring `MENSURA_SANDBOX_DIR`; factory now `mkdtemp(dir=parent)`), `backup_service.py` (inject `retention_policy`, add `prune()`, best-effort prune after each successful create), `backup_repositories.py` + `persistence/repositories/backup.py` (add `delete`), `job_service.py` (inject `retention_policy`, add `prune_jobs()` with retry-lineage protection), `job_repositories.py` + `persistence/repositories/job.py` (add `delete`), `main.py` (build backup/job policies from env + inject, construct `VerificationSandboxSweeper` on `app.state`, new `enable_startup_maintenance` flag + `_run_startup_maintenance`, `create_sql_app` enables it), `migrations/env.py` (**real bug fix:** `fileConfig(..., disable_existing_loggers=False)` so startup migrations no longer silently disable Core's own loggers).
  - **Edited (tests/docs):** `tests/test_durable_sql_app.py` (+2 integration tests: startup sweep, post-create backup retention), `README.md`, `services/core/README.md`, this journal.
- **Sandbox cleanup strategy + scope:** a once-per-process sweep in the durable startup lifespan (before the worker starts and before traffic). Single-process is the safety lever — no verification can be in flight, so any `mensura-verification-*` directory present is orphaned by a prior process. It (1) deletes only directories whose name carries the Mensura prefix **and** whose layout is exactly what the factory creates (empty, or one `worktree` child) — never a symlink, never a prefixed dir with unexpected contents (those are logged + skipped, never deleted); (2) then runs Git's own `git worktree prune` per configured workspace to drop stale `.git/worktrees` metadata (dirs removed first so prune sees the missing working tree); (3) treats every failure as a logged warning, never a startup abort; (4) logs inspected/removed/skipped/worktrees_pruned. Parent dir is the system temp dir or `MENSURA_SANDBOX_DIR` (both factory and sweeper agree). Gated by `enable_startup_maintenance` (only `create_sql_app`), so the many unit-test apps never scan the real temp dir.
- **Retention thresholds + defaults:** one union-of-keeps `RetentionPolicy` — keep if within newest `keep_at_least` OR within newest `max_count` OR newer than `max_age_days`; prune only when it fails all three. Either dimension `0` = inactive; **both `0` = disabled (prune nothing)** is the documented off-switch. Defaults (conservative): **backups** `MENSURA_BACKUP_RETENTION_COUNT=10`, `MENSURA_BACKUP_RETENTION_DAYS=30`, `keep_at_least=1`; **terminal jobs** `MENSURA_JOB_RETENTION_COUNT=200`, `MENSURA_JOB_RETENTION_DAYS=30`, `keep_at_least=0`. A backup count `< 1` is clamped to `1`. Cadence: backups pruned after each successful create *and* at startup; terminal jobs pruned at startup. No scheduler/cron.
- **Pruned vs. never-pruned:** PRUNED — completed/failed **backups** beyond policy (on-disk file unlinked *before* the DB row; a file-unlink failure skips the row delete so a surviving row always still refers to its file) and **terminal jobs** (succeeded/failed) beyond policy. NEVER PRUNED — core domain artifacts (tasks, runs, proposals, verifications, applications, undos); **queued/running jobs**; the user's **only/newest backup** (`keep_at_least=1`); and any terminal job still referenced by another job as its retry parent/root (lineage integrity). All deletions are best-effort (warn, never crash).
- **What now works end-to-end (manual durable run, real `create_app` + migrations + worker + lifespan across a simulated restart):** proc #1 ran 4 `backup_create` jobs → backups bounded to 2 (post-create prune) with matching DB-rows and on-disk files, and 4 succeeded terminal jobs accumulated; a crash then seeded `mensura-verification-crashed/worktree` plus an unrelated dir; proc #2 restarted on the same DB/backup/sandbox dirs → startup maintenance removed the orphaned sandbox, kept the unrelated dir, held backups at 2, and pruned terminal jobs to 1. The real-git prune path (worktree metadata dropped via `git worktree prune`, `git worktree list` back to 1) is covered by a unit test.
- **Verification:** Core `213 passed` (182 prior + 10 sweep unit, 19 retention unit + service, 2 durable-SQL integration). `ruff check src tests` clean; all new + my added code is `ruff format`-clean (the 2 remaining format flags are pre-existing drift in untouched regions of `backup_service.py::restore_backup` / `job_service.py::retry`, consistent with the cycle-21/22 note — Guard uses `check`, not `format`). No OpenAPI change (still 42 operations / 37 paths — retention/sweep are internal). Fixed a real latent operability bug along the way: startup Alembic migrations were disabling all already-created loggers (`fileConfig` default), which would have silenced Core's own backup/job/sweep/retention logs.
- **Intentionally deferred:** retention for other artifacts (SSE buffer is already bounded in-memory; verification/application/undo artifacts are core history and out of scope); a user-facing retention/prune API or Studio surface (env-configured + startup/post-create automatic only); periodic (non-startup) job pruning within a long-running process; per-workspace backup grouping (backups are global DB snapshots, so retention is global); pruning old *queued* jobs (never — operationally live); cross-process/multi-instance sandbox coordination (single-process assumption); the repo-wide `ruff format` pass.
- **Next best slice:** the repo-wide `ruff format` pass (now the largest remaining untracked drift, spanning cycle-16→22 files) paired with switching Guard's `lint` to also run `ruff format --check`, so format is enforced going forward; then the optional read/write reservation letting standalone Guard exclude live-tree writers. A Studio "maintenance" panel surfacing the last sweep/retention summary + current thresholds is a natural small UX follow-up once a metrics/summary endpoint exists.

### 2026-07-21 — Start cycle 24: Mensura Vault MVP (indexing + semantic retrieval + architecture summary)

- Intent (product expansion, MVP-sized): deliver the first real Vault layer — a workspace can be indexed into persisted memory items + chunks with metadata and searchable content; users can query Vault to retrieve relevant code/docs; Core can generate a basic architecture summary from indexed material. This is Phase 3 of `mensura_roadmap.md` (file/document ingestion, embeddings, semantic search, architecture summary generation) and the `/vault/index`, `/vault/search`, `/vault/memory/:id`, `/vault/summarize` endpoints of `mensura_api_outline.md`. Keep local-first defaults; preserve current Core safety + persistence guarantees; do NOT attempt full graph memory, team sharing, branch-aware snapshots, or polished UX.
- Re-read the existing Vault surface before designing. Today's Vault is a **read-only deterministic inventory** (`vault_inventory.py` `LocalVaultInventoryBuilder` walk with `VaultInventoryRules` exclusions + text/binary classification + language-by-extension, `vault_service.py` list/preview, `vault_repositories.py`/`persistence/repositories/vault.py` latest-per-workspace snapshot, `POST/GET /workspaces/{id}/vault/inventory|files|files/content`). The new indexing layer is **additive** and reuses the inventory's exclusion rules, language map, and text/binary classification; the inventory endpoints are untouched.
- **Data model (new, migration 006, in the existing SQLite path).** Latest-per-workspace, mirroring the inventory snapshot pattern: `vault_index_snapshots` (unique `workspace_id`, status, `indexed_at`, JSON summary, item/chunk counts) → `vault_memory_items` (FK snapshot, cascade; `workspace_id`, `path`, `source_type` code|doc|config, `language`, `digest` sha256, `size_bytes`, `chunk_count`, `indexed_at`) → `vault_chunks` (FK memory item, cascade; `chunk_index`, `start_line`, `end_line`, `char_count`, `digest`, `text`, JSON sparse `embedding`, plus denormalized `path`/`source_type`/`language` for single-table search + hit construction). Re-indexing replaces the workspace's snapshot (cascade-deletes its items+chunks) exactly like the inventory `save_latest`.
- **Chunking (simple + explicit).** Docs/markdown/text split by markdown headings + blank-line paragraph boundaries into ≤~1500-char chunks; code/config split into bounded fixed line windows (≤80 lines AND ≤1500 chars). Every chunk retains `start_line`/`end_line` (1-based inclusive) + `char_count` + content `digest` back to its source memory item. Whitespace-only chunks dropped; a file that yields none is skipped (`empty`). Bounds: `MAX_INDEXED_FILE_BYTES` 1 MB (skip `too_large`, smaller than the 5 MB preview cap and explicit), `MAX_CHUNKS_PER_FILE` 200.
- **Retrieval (honest, local-first, dependency-free).** No embedding library is available (no numpy/torch), and network/model downloads violate local-first. So the "embedding" is a **deterministic local hashing vectorizer**: tokenize → hash unigrams+bigrams with `blake2b` (NOT Python's per-process-salted `hash()`, so persisted vectors are stable across restarts) into `EMBEDDING_DIM=512` buckets → term-frequency counts → L2-normalize → sparse `{bucket: weight}`. Search embeds the query the same way and ranks chunks by cosine similarity (dot of two normalized sparse maps over shared buckets) with a small exact-substring boost. This is a lexical vector model, not neural embeddings — documented as such — behind a pluggable `Embedder` protocol so a real model can be dropped in later without a schema change. Vectors are persisted so search is reproducible from the index alone (not the live tree).
- **Architecture summary.** Pure heuristic over indexed memory items (`vault_summary.py`): file/code/doc/config counts + total bytes, top languages, top-level directory "modules" (file count + bytes + dominant language), detected technologies from marker files (package.json→Node, pyproject/requirements→Python, Cargo.toml→Rust, go.mod→Go, Dockerfile→Docker, tsconfig→TypeScript, …), and heuristic entry points (main.py/index.ts/main.rs/…). Bounded, honest, not AI-generated.
- **API (additive, top-level `/vault` per the spec outline).** `POST /vault/index` {workspaceId} → snapshot; `GET /vault/indexes/{workspace_id}` → latest snapshot (404 if not built); `POST /vault/search` {workspaceId, query, limit?, sourceType?} → ranked hits; `GET /vault/memory/{memory_id}` → item + its chunks; `POST /vault/summarize` {workspaceId} → architecture summary. Bounded, explicit camelCase schemas; new structured problems for index-not-built / memory-not-found.
- **Safety/exclusions.** Reuse the inventory's directory/file exclusions (.git, node_modules, venv, dist, build, secrets, binaries, …); never traverse symlinks or outside the workspace root; explicit 1 MB size cap; skip binary/too-large/unsupported/empty files and record why (bounded skip sample + counts by reason in the summary).
- **Studio:** intentionally deferred this cycle (Core-first MVP; keep scope bounded). Documented as a next slice.
- Follow-up order: exceptions → `vault_index_models.py` → `vault_index_repositories.py` (dataclasses+Protocol+InMemory) → `vault_indexer.py` (embedder/chunkers/walk) → `vault_summary.py` → `vault_index_service.py` → persistence rows + migration 006 + SQL repo + exports → API router/deps/problems/router-include → `main.py` wiring + `conftest.py` → tests (indexer, service, summary, API, durable-SQL integration, OpenAPI paths) → READMEs + this journal → full pytest + ruff.

### 2026-07-21 — Complete cycle 24: Mensura Vault MVP (indexing + semantic retrieval + architecture summary)

- **Files changed (11 new, 13 edited):**
  - **New (src, 7):** `vault_index_models.py` (bounded Pydantic contracts + enums), `vault_index_repositories.py` (internal `IndexedMemoryItem`/`IndexedChunk`/`ChunkVector`/`VaultIndexRecord` dataclasses + `VaultIndexRepository` Protocol + `InMemoryVaultIndexRepository`), `vault_indexer.py` (`HashingEmbedder`, `cosine_similarity`, `classify_source_type`, `chunk_document`/`chunk_code`, `LocalVaultIndexer` walk), `vault_summary.py` (heuristic architecture summary), `vault_index_service.py` (`VaultIndexService`), `persistence/repositories/vault_index.py` (`SqlVaultIndexRepository`), `api/routers/vault_index.py` (top-level `/vault` router).
  - **New (migration, 1):** `migrations/versions/006_vault_index.py` (3 tables + indexes; head is now `006`).
  - **New (tests, 3):** `tests/test_vault_indexer.py` (23), `tests/test_vault_index_service.py` (12), `tests/test_vault_index_api.py` (12).
  - **Edited (src, 7):** `exceptions.py` (`VaultIndexNotBuiltError`, `VaultMemoryItemNotFoundError`), `persistence/models.py` (3 Row classes + `from_record` + workspace `vault_indexes` relationship + summary TypeAdapter), `persistence/__init__.py` (export `SqlVaultIndexRepository`), `api/dependencies.py` (`VaultIndexServiceDependency`), `api/problems.py` (2 handlers + type consts), `api/router.py` (include `vault_index`), `main.py` (build `HashingEmbedder` + `LocalVaultIndexer` + repo, wire `app.state.vault_index_service`; new `vault_indexer`/`vault_index_repository` params).
  - **Edited (tests/docs, 3+3):** `tests/test_openapi.py` (+5 paths), `tests/test_persistence.py` (+3 tables), `tests/test_durable_sql_app.py` (+1 restart-durability integration test), `README.md`, `services/core/README.md`, this journal.
- **Vault data model chosen:** latest-per-workspace, three durable tables in the existing SQLite path (migration 006): `vault_index_snapshots` (unique `workspace_id`, status, `indexed_at`, JSON summary, item/chunk counts) → `vault_memory_items` (one per indexed file: `path`, `source_type`, `language`, sha256 `digest`, `size_bytes`, `chunk_count`, `indexed_at`) → `vault_chunks` (one per chunk: `chunk_index`, `start_line`/`end_line`, `char_count`, sha256 `digest`, `text`, sparse JSON `embedding`, plus denormalized `path`/`source_type`/`language` so search is a single indexed-column table scan and hits carry item context without a join). FK cascades mean re-indexing (which deletes the prior snapshot) drops its items and chunks; deleting a workspace drops its index. Chunk embeddings never cross the API boundary — the service maps records to bounded camelCase models.
- **Chunking strategy chosen:** docs (`.md`/`.rst`/`.txt`/…) split on markdown headings and blank-line paragraph boundaries into ≤~1500-char chunks (hard cap 2×, ≤1 line overflow); code/config split into bounded fixed line windows (≤80 lines AND ≤~1500 chars). Chunks trim blank edges, carry 1-based inclusive line ranges + `charCount` + content digest, and are capped at 200/file. Empty/whitespace-only files yield no chunks and are skipped.
- **Retrieval strategy chosen (documented honestly):** a **local, dependency-free lexical vector model** — tokenize → hash unigrams+bigrams with `blake2b` into 512 buckets → term-frequency → L2-normalize → sparse vector; rank by cosine similarity (dot over shared buckets) with a small exact-substring boost, optional `sourceType` filter, `limit` 1–50. `blake2b` (not per-process-salted `hash()`) keeps persisted vectors stable across restarts, so search is reproducible from the index alone. Explicitly **not** neural/semantic embeddings; sits behind a pluggable `Embedder` protocol so a real model can replace it with no schema/API change.
- **What now works end-to-end (verified on real material through the durable `create_sql_app` path):** indexed `services/core` itself → 131 memory items / 625 chunks (128 code, 1 doc, 2 config; 3 skipped: 2 `empty`, 1 `unsupported_type`); `POST /vault/search "workspace write reservation"` top-ranked the reservation test + the README reservation sections, `"verification sandbox git worktree"` surfaced `verification_sweep.py`; `POST /vault/summarize` reported the real modules (`src` 102 Python, `tests` 27 Python, `(root)` 2 TOML), technologies (`Alembic`, `Python`), and entry point `src/mensura_core/main.py`. A dedicated integration test indexes through the real SQLite+Alembic path with one app instance and then searches/reads/summarizes from a **second** instance on the same DB file, proving the index is durable across a restart (not just in-process).
- **Verification:** Core `261 passed` (213 prior + 23 indexer + 12 service + 12 API + 1 durable integration; `test_openapi`/`test_persistence` fixed-set assertions extended for the 5 new paths + 3 new tables). `ruff check src tests` clean; all 11 new files are `ruff format`-clean. Migrations reach head `006`; the durable table set now includes `vault_index_snapshots`/`vault_memory_items`/`vault_chunks`. No existing endpoint, artifact, or safety guarantee changed — indexing is read-only over the workspace and writes only Core's SQLite DB.
- **Intentionally deferred:** Studio surface (Core-first MVP — no indexing/search/summary UI this cycle); real neural/semantic embeddings (interface is pluggable); full graph memory + `POST /vault/graph/query`, linked task memory, branch-aware snapshots, cross-workspace shared memory; incremental/watched/background re-indexing (index is manual + synchronous, full-replace); binary/large-file content extraction; retention/pruning of old Vault indexes (only-latest-per-workspace already bounds growth to one index/workspace, but a stale index for a deleted-then-recreated workspace is not swept).
- **Next best slice:** a minimal Studio Vault surface — an "Index workspace" trigger + status/summary card and a search box with ranked results linking to memory-item chunks — now that the Core endpoints exist and are durable; then swapping the hashing embedder for a real local embedding model behind the existing `Embedder` protocol (the schema already stores per-chunk vectors) to move from lexical-vector to genuinely semantic retrieval. `POST /vault/summarize` feeding the context-pack/task flow (so an architecture summary can seed a run) is a natural follow-on once Studio can display it.

### 2026-07-21 — Start cycle 25: Studio Vault surface (index trigger + status/summary + search + architecture summary)

- Intent (product/UX, MVP-sized, Studio-only): expose the cycle-24 Vault index/search/summary Core endpoints in Studio so a user can, from the desktop app, (1) trigger indexing for the active workspace, (2) see indexed/not-indexed status + last-indexed time + summary counts, (3) run a ranked search with a `sourceType` filter and open a chunk detail, and (4) view a basic architecture summary. Reuse the existing Core API + schema unchanged (no Core changes expected); keep the UI honest about MVP limits (lexical-vector "semantic" retrieval, manual full-replace indexing). No graph viz, no linked task memory, no branch-aware/shared memory.
- Re-read the ground truth in code at commit `93e5366` + the uncommitted cycle-24 Core tree: the new endpoints are `POST /api/v1/vault/index` {workspaceId}→`VaultIndexSnapshot` (201), `GET /api/v1/vault/indexes/{workspace_id}`→snapshot (404 `urn:mensura:problem:vault-index-not-built` when absent), `POST /api/v1/vault/search` {workspaceId, query, limit?≤50, sourceType?}→`VaultSearchResponse` (ranked `hits[]` with `path`/`sourceType`/`language`/`chunkIndex`/`startLine`/`endLine`/`score`/`snippet`, `strategy:"lexical-vector-cosine"`, `total`/`returned`), `GET /api/v1/vault/memory/{memory_id}`→`VaultMemoryItemDetail` (item + chunks, 404 `vault-memory-not-found`), `POST /api/v1/vault/summarize` {workspaceId}→`VaultArchitectureSummary` (counts, `languages[]`, `modules[]`, `technologies[]`, `entryPoints[]`). All camelCase over the wire (verified in `test_vault_index_api.py`). Empty/blank query → 422. These are DISTINCT from the older read-only inventory endpoints (`/workspaces/{id}/vault/inventory|files|files/content`) that the existing `VaultPanel.tsx` already surfaces.
- **Entry-point decision:** a NEW dedicated full-width **"Vault memory" panel** (`features/vault/VaultIndexPanel.tsx`, eyebrow "Semantic index (MVP)") added to the existing single-view dashboard grid as a sibling BELOW the current "Vault inventory" panel — NOT a new nav route (Studio still has no router; the sidebar is a static "Core overview") and NOT merged into the inventory panel (that is a different feature: deterministic file inventory). This keeps both Vault features legible, reuses `Panel`/`AsyncState`/`ProblemDetailsView`/`badge`/`button` conventions, and needs zero navigation refactor. Keyed by `activeWorkspaceId` like `GuardPanel`/`VaultPanel` so all local state resets on workspace switch.
- **Status/summary display:** `getVaultIndex` query (retry off); a `vault-index-not-built` error is treated as a neutral "Not indexed" empty state with an index prompt (mirrors the inventory panel's not-built handling), any other error → `ProblemDetailsView`. When indexed: an "Indexed" badge + last-indexed timestamp + a counts grid (memory items, chunks, code/doc/config files, total size) + language badges + skipped count. Indexing runs as a mutation with a disabled "Indexing…" button + spinner status row; failures render bounded via `ProblemDetailsView`.
- **Search + navigation:** search is a submit-driven mutation (query input + optional `sourceType` select, `limit=20`); results list shows `#rank`, path, sourceType/language badge, line range, score, and snippet in descending order; no-results shows "No matching chunks found" with a refine hint. Because Studio has no code editor yet, "navigation to file" is implemented as the task-sanctioned first step: clicking a result opens a **chunk detail side panel** via `getVaultMemoryItem(memoryItemId)` showing the memory item metadata + all its chunks with line ranges, highlighting the hit chunk. Architecture summary is a separate on-demand `summarize` mutation rendering modules/technologies/languages/entry points/counts.
- **Honesty copy:** an "About Vault" `<details>` disclosure in the panel stating indexing is manual + full-replace (no incremental/watch), search is a local lexical-vector model (not neural embeddings) with a small exact-substring boost, results are approximate, and large/binary files are skipped by design.
- **Testing plan:** `VaultIndexPanel.test.tsx` — not-indexed empty state (no Core call when no workspace); click "Index workspace" → pending "Indexing…" → indexed status + counts (mocked `indexVaultWorkspace`); render mocked search hits (paths/snippets/line ranges/rank visible); click a hit → `getVaultMemoryItem` called with the right id → chunk detail shown (navigation via test double); no-results empty state; generate architecture summary. Focused, deterministic, no timers.
- **Anticipated changes (Studio + shared-types only):** new `packages/shared-types/src/vault-index.ts` (+`.test.ts`, +index barrel export, rebuild `dist`); `apps/studio/src/api/coreClient.ts` (5 methods + interface); `app/queryClient.ts` (query keys); `test/render.tsx` (test-client defaults); `features/vault/VaultIndexPanel.tsx` (+`.test.tsx`); `app/App.tsx` (mount panel); `styles.css` (grid area + section styles); `apps/studio/README.md`, `services/core/README.md`, this journal. Core API/schema/migrations: expected UNCHANGED (only add denormalized fields if a Studio need surfaces a gap — none anticipated since search hits already carry path/language/sourceType/line ranges).
- Follow-up order: shared-types module + test + barrel + dist build → coreClient methods + interface → queryClient keys → render.tsx defaults → VaultIndexPanel → VaultIndexPanel.test → App wiring → styles → READMEs → `pnpm --filter @mensura/shared-types build` + full `pnpm typecheck && pnpm test && pnpm build` → manual index→summary→search→open against a real repo via the durable Core app.

### 2026-07-21 — Complete cycle 25: Studio Vault surface (index trigger + status/summary + search + architecture summary)

  - **New (Studio, 2):** `apps/studio/src/features/vault/VaultIndexPanel.tsx` (the panel), `apps/studio/src/features/vault/VaultIndexPanel.test.tsx` (7 behavior tests).
  - **Edited (Studio+types, 6):** `packages/shared-types/src/index.ts` (barrel export + rebuilt `dist`), `apps/studio/src/api/coreClient.ts` (5 methods + interface: `indexVaultWorkspace`, `getVaultIndex`, `searchVault`, `getVaultMemoryItem`, `summarizeVaultWorkspace`), `app/queryClient.ts` (`vaultIndex`/`vaultMemoryItem` keys), `test/render.tsx` (5 test-client defaults), `app/App.tsx` (mount `VaultIndexPanel` in a new `dashboard-grid__vault-index` full-width area below the inventory panel, keyed by workspace), `styles.css` (grid area + responsive + `vault-index-*`/`vault-hit`/`vault-chunk`/`vault-module` styles).
  - **Edited (docs, 3):** `apps/studio/README.md` (Current-UI bullet + a "how to use" paragraph + intro clause), `services/core/README.md` (Vault section now notes the Studio panel; reworded the deferred list), this journal.
- **Entry-point design chosen:** a NEW dedicated full-width **"Vault memory" panel** (eyebrow "Semantic index (MVP)"), a sibling BELOW the existing read-only "Vault inventory" panel in the single-view dashboard grid. NOT a nav route (Studio still has no router — the sidebar is a static "Core overview") and NOT merged into the inventory panel (a distinct feature: deterministic file inventory). It reuses `Panel`/`AsyncState`/`ProblemDetailsView`/`badge`/`button`, is keyed by `activeWorkspaceId` (all local state resets on workspace switch, like `GuardPanel`/`VaultPanel`), and needed zero navigation refactor.
- **How index status + summary are displayed:** a `getVaultIndex` query (retry off, enabled only with a workspace). A `vault-index-not-built` 404 is treated as a neutral **"Not indexed"** empty state with an index prompt (mirrors the inventory panel's not-built handling) — any other error renders via `ProblemDetailsView`. When indexed: an **"Indexed"** `badge--clean` + last-indexed `<time>` (deterministic `Intl` UTC format) + a `vault-index-counts` grid (memory items, chunks, code/doc/config, size, skipped) + language badges. Indexing is a mutation with a disabled **"Indexing…"** button and a spinner status row ("Core is reading and chunking workspace files (full re-index)…"); on success it `setQueryData`s the snapshot (no invalidate/refetch) and resets stale search/summary/detail. The toolbar button reads "Index workspace" → "Re-index" once indexed.
- **Search UI + navigation behavior:** search is a submit-driven `useMutation` (idle→"Enter a query…" empty state) with a query `input[type=search]` + optional `code`/`doc`/`config` `select`, `limit=20`. Results are an ordered list of hits showing **#rank**, path, source-type/language badges, `lines A–B`, `score` (3-dp), and a 2-line-clamped snippet, plus a `Showing R of T · strategy <code>` meta line. **Navigation** (Studio has no code editor yet, so the task-sanctioned first step): clicking a hit sets `{memoryItemId, chunkId}`, which enables a `getVaultMemoryItem` query and renders a **chunk-detail side pane** — item metadata (path/type/language/size) + all chunks with line ranges, the hit chunk highlighted (`vault-chunk--match` + a "Match" badge) and an honest hint that this is the indexed chunk, not an editor. No-results shows "No matching chunks found for '<query>'. Try different or broader terms." Architecture summary is a separate on-demand `summarize` mutation → counts, technologies, entry points, and a top-level modules list.
- **Honest capability copy:** an "About Vault memory" `<details>` disclosure states indexing is manual + full-replace (no incremental/watch), search is a **local lexical vector model, not neural embeddings** (approximate matching, small exact-substring boost), and large/binary files are skipped by design.
- **What now works end-to-end (verified over real HTTP against the durable `create_sql_app` on a live socket, indexing `packages/shared-types` as a workspace — no mocks):** `POST /api/v1/vault/index {workspaceId}` → 36 memory items / 66 chunks (34 code, 0 doc, 2 config; 0 skipped; languages TypeScript 34, JSON 2); `GET /api/v1/vault/indexes/{id}` → 200 with matching `workspaceId`; `POST /api/v1/vault/search {query,limit:20,sourceType:"code"}` → `strategy:"lexical-vector-cosine"`, total 55/returned 20, top hit `src/index.ts` lines 1–18, **all hits `sourceType==code`** (filter honored); `GET /api/v1/vault/memory/{id}` → item + chunk with all fields; `POST /api/v1/vault/summarize` → fileCount 36, technologies `[Node.js, TypeScript]`, entryPoints `[src/index.ts]`, modules `src`(34,TS)/`(root)`(2,JSON). The not-indexed path returns **404 `application/problem+json` type `urn:mensura:problem:vault-index-not-built`** (exactly the constant the panel's "Not indexed" state keys on) and a blank query returns 422. **Every response field name matched the new TypeScript interfaces exactly**, confirming the Studio↔Core contract with no Core change.

Studio `76 passed` across 19 files (69 prior + 7 new VaultIndexPanel tests: no-workspace no-call, not-indexed empty state, index→"Indexing…"→indexed-with-counts, ranked results with path/line-range/snippet/rank, chunk-detail navigation via `getVaultMemoryItem`, no-results empty state, on-demand architecture summary). `tsc --noEmit` clean under the strict base config (`exactOptionalPropertyTypes`, `noUncheckedIndexedAccess`); `vite build` clean (115 modules, 331.68 kB / 91.74 kB gz JS, 35.52 kB CSS). Plus the live durable-server HTTP smoke above.
