### 2026-07-22 — Start cycle 26: Studio Vault search-hit → file-view navigation (open + scroll/highlight line range)

- Intent (product/UX, Studio-only): turn the cycle-25 Vault search from "preview-only chunk cards" into an actionable navigation tool — clicking a search hit opens the corresponding file content in a real (read-only) Studio file view that shows the file path, line-numbered content, and scrolls to / highlights the hit's `startLine–endLine`. Reuse existing Core/Studio capabilities; NO new Core schema/persistence; no full editor (no editing, no syntax highlighting, no multi-tab, no annotations).
- Re-read the ground truth in code at commit `8c15b7c`. Two existing content-fetch endpoints were candidates for the file view's content source:
  1. `getVaultFilePreview(workspaceId, path)` → `GET /workspaces/{id}/vault/files/content` (the read-only **inventory** preview surface the existing `VaultPanel` already uses). BUT `vault_service.get_file_preview` (a) `_require_inventory(...)` — depends on a **separately-built inventory snapshot**, not the index the search hit came from (a user can index without building the inventory → the hit's file view would 404 `vault-inventory-not-built`); and (b) caps at `PREVIEW_LIMIT_BYTES = 16 KiB`, so for larger files the hit's line range is frequently **past the truncation point** and cannot be scrolled to. Poor fit for reliably "landing on the hit line."
  2. `getVaultMemoryItem(memoryItemId)` → `GET /vault/memory/{id}` → `VaultMemoryItemDetail` = `{ item, chunks[] }`, already fetched today by the panel's chunk-detail pane. Each `VaultChunk` carries exact 1-based inclusive `startLine`/`endLine` + `text`, and the hit's `chunkId`/`startLine`/`endLine` reference one of these chunks. This is the **same durable index snapshot the hit came from** — line ranges always align, the hit's lines are always present (up to 200 chunks/file ≈ 16k lines, vs. 16 KiB), and there is no cross-panel inventory dependency.
- **Decision (content source):** reconstruct a line-numbered read-only file view from the **index memory item's chunks** (`getVaultMemoryItem`, already wired), NOT the inventory preview endpoint. Rationale: consistency with the hit's own snapshot (exact line alignment, hit lines guaranteed present), no 16 KiB truncation gap, no dependency on a separately-built inventory, zero new Core surface. `getVaultFilePreview` was considered and rejected as the primary source for the two reasons above (documented so a future cycle can revisit if a live-re-read view is wanted). This evolves the existing chunk-detail pane (chunk cards) into a single continuous line-numbered file view.
- **Reconstruction algorithm:** sort chunks by `chunkIndex`; concatenate their text as lines numbered from each chunk's `startLine`; insert an explicit "⋯ lines X–Y not indexed ⋯" gap marker when a chunk's `startLine` jumps past the previous chunk's `endLine + 1` (docs drop whitespace-only chunks; code >200 chunks is capped) so line numbers stay honest; defensively clamp overlaps so line numbers are monotonic; drop the single trailing empty line from each chunk's terminal `\n`. Highlight every line belonging to the hit's chunk (`chunk.id === hit.chunkId`, i.e. lines `hit.startLine…hit.endLine`); attach a ref to the first highlighted line and `scrollIntoView({ block: "center" })` (guarded — jsdom has no `scrollIntoView`).
- **UX:** the search-results list is unchanged; clicking a hit now stores the full hit (`memoryItemId, chunkId, path, sourceType, language, startLine, endLine`) and the right-hand pane heading becomes **"File view"** rendering `VaultFileView` (primary). Header shows the path (`code`), source-type/language badges, a "Matched lines A–B" caption, and compact size/chunk-count metadata (preserves the old chunk-detail metadata). A lightweight **"← Back to results"** button clears the selection (useful when the layout stacks on narrow screens). Honest hint: read-only, reconstructed from the durable index (not a live re-read), no editor.
- **Empty/error states (bounded, no raw exceptions):** no selection → "Select a result to open its file here."; loading → "Opening file…"; **stale hit after re-index** (`getVaultMemoryItem` 404 `urn:mensura:problem:vault-memory-not-found`) → a bounded "This result is stale — its file is no longer in the current index. Re-run the search." with a back affordance; any other error → `ProblemDetailsView`; detail loaded but the matched chunk absent / hit range outside indexed content → a bounded "Matched lines A–B are no longer in this file's indexed content." note while still rendering available content; zero chunks → "No indexed content for this file." Binary/too-large files are never indexed, so they never appear as hits (no separate handling needed).
- **Anticipated changes (Studio + docs only; NO Core src/schema/migration, NO shared-types change — all fields already exist on `VaultMemoryItemDetail`/`VaultChunk`/`VaultSearchHit`):** new `features/vault/VaultFileView.tsx` (+`.test.tsx`); edit `features/vault/VaultIndexPanel.tsx` (expand `SelectedHit`, swap chunk-detail pane for the file view + stale handling + clear-selection, remove the now-superseded `ChunkDetail`/`ChunkView`) and its `.test.tsx` (rewrite the "chunk detail" test as a "file view" test: path header + line numbers + highlighted matched line; add a stale-hit test); `styles.css` (`.vault-file-view*` + responsive); `apps/studio/README.md`; a small `services/core/README.md` note (no API behavior change — Studio reuses `GET /vault/memory/{id}`); this journal.
- Follow-up order: VaultFileView + test → VaultIndexPanel rewire + test updates → styles → typecheck/test/build → READMEs → this journal (after) → manual smoke against the durable Core app (index a repo, search, click a hit, confirm the file view scrolls to and highlights the hit lines, and a re-index makes an old hit's file view show the bounded stale message).

### 2026-07-22 — Complete cycle 26: Studio Vault search-hit → file-view navigation (open + scroll/highlight line range)

- **Files changed (2 new, 6 edited; Studio + docs only — NO Core src/schema/migration/dependency change and NO shared-types change, the cycle constraint held; all needed fields already existed on `VaultMemoryItemDetail`/`VaultChunk`/`VaultSearchHit`):**
  - **New (Studio, 2):** `apps/studio/src/features/vault/VaultFileView.tsx` (the read-only line-numbered file viewer + exported `VaultFileHit` type + `buildFile`/`splitChunkLines` reconstruction helpers), `apps/studio/src/features/vault/VaultFileView.test.tsx` (4 unit tests).
  - **Edited (Studio, 4):** `features/vault/VaultIndexPanel.tsx` (expanded `SelectedHit` to carry `path`/`sourceType`/`language`/`startLine`/`endLine`; the right-hand pane heading is now **"File view"** and renders `VaultFileView` on success; added stale-hit detection `isMemoryStale` (`vault-memory-not-found`) → bounded message + back affordance; added `onClearHit`; removed the now-superseded `ChunkDetail`/`ChunkView`; dropped the unused `VaultChunk` import), `features/vault/VaultIndexPanel.test.tsx` (rewrote the old "chunk detail" test as a "line-numbered file view + highlight + back" test; added a stale-hit test), `styles.css` (replaced the now-dead `.vault-chunk*` block with `.vault-file-view*` / `.vault-file-line*` / `.vault-file-gap` styles), plus the responsive breakpoint already stacks `.vault-index-layout`.
  - **Edited (docs, 2):** `apps/studio/README.md` (feature bullet + the how-to paragraph now describe the file view), `services/core/README.md` (Vault section notes Studio's file view reuses `GET /vault/memory/{id}` with no new endpoint + the stale-hit 404 mapping), this journal.
- **File-view approach chosen — NEW minimal read-only viewer, content reused from an existing Core endpoint (NOT the inventory preview endpoint):** clicking a hit renders `VaultFileView`, which reconstructs a line-numbered rendering of the file from the memory item's indexed chunks fetched via the already-wired `getVaultMemoryItem` (`GET /vault/memory/{id}`). **Why not `getVaultFilePreview`** (the inventory text-preview surface the task nudged toward): `vault_service.get_file_preview` (a) `_require_inventory(...)` — depends on a *separately-built inventory snapshot* the search hit did not come from (index-without-inventory → the file view would 404 `vault-inventory-not-built`), and (b) caps at `PREVIEW_LIMIT_BYTES = 16 KiB` so a hit past the truncation point in a larger file could never be scrolled to. The index chunks come from the **same durable snapshot as the hit**, so line ranges always align, the hit's lines are always present (up to 200 chunks/file ≈ 16k lines), there is no cross-panel inventory dependency, and stale-after-re-index is the existing `vault-memory-not-found` 404. Verified the linchpin in Core: a search hit's `chunkId` is `ChunkVector.chunk_id`, which is set to the chunk row's `id` in **both** the in-memory (`vault_index_repositories.py:147`) and SQL (`persistence/repositories/vault_index.py:84`) repos — identical to the `id` `get_memory_item` returns on each chunk — so the highlight matches on real data.
- **How line-range navigation/highlighting works:** `buildFile(detail, hit.chunkId)` sorts chunks by `chunkIndex`, concatenates their text as lines numbered from each chunk's `startLine`, inserts an explicit `⋯ lines X–Y not indexed ⋯` marker whenever a chunk's `startLine` jumps past the previous chunk's `endLine + 1` (docs drop whitespace-only chunks; code past the 200-chunk cap), defensively clamps overlaps so line numbers stay monotonic, and drops the single trailing empty line from each chunk's terminal `\n`. Every line whose chunk `id === hit.chunkId` is flagged `match` (⇒ a green left-accent + tinted row via `.vault-file-line--match`, i.e. exactly the hit's `startLine…endLine`), and the first such line is flagged `firstMatch` and given a ref that a `useEffect` scrolls into view with `scrollIntoView({ block: "center" })` (optional-chained so jsdom's missing implementation is a no-op). The header shows the path, source-type/language badges, a "Matched lines A–B" caption, and compact size/chunk-count metadata (preserving the old chunk-detail metadata); a `← Back to results` button clears the selection.
- **Empty/error states (bounded, no raw exceptions):** no selection → "Select a result to open its file here."; loading → "Opening file…"; **stale hit** (`vault-memory-not-found` 404) → "This result is stale — its file is no longer in the current index. Re-run the search…" with a back affordance (raw problem title is NOT surfaced); any other error → `ProblemDetailsView`; matched chunk absent though the item loaded (or hit range outside indexed content) → a bounded "Matched lines A–B are no longer in this file's indexed content." note while still rendering available lines; zero chunks → "No indexed content for this file." Binary/too-large files are never indexed so never appear as hits.
- **What now works end-to-end:** from the Studio "Vault memory" panel, running a search and clicking a ranked hit now opens a read-only, line-numbered **File view** of that file (reconstructed from the durable index), auto-scrolls to the hit's line block, and highlights exactly `hit.startLine…endLine`; non-indexed gaps are shown explicitly; `← Back to results` returns to the results-only state; a hit whose memory item was dropped by a re-index shows the bounded stale message instead of a raw error. Vault search is now an actionable file-navigation tool rather than preview-only. (Validated by the component + panel tests below and by reading the Core contract the view depends on; the underlying `GET /vault/memory/{id}` shape was already verified over real HTTP in cycle 25, unchanged here.)
- **Verification:** Studio `81 passed` across 20 files (was 76/19: +4 `VaultFileView` unit tests — line-numbered render + gap marker + hit-chunk highlight, back callback, missing-match note with content still shown, empty-content message; +1 stale-hit panel test; the old "chunk detail" panel test rewritten in place as a file-view test asserting the fetched memory-item id, the unique line-2 content, the "Matched lines 1–2" caption, the `.vault-file-line--match` highlight class, and back-to-results). `tsc --noEmit` clean under the strict base config (`exactOptionalPropertyTypes`, `noUncheckedIndexedAccess`); `vite build` clean (116 modules, up from 115 — the new viewer; JS 333.93 kB / 92.55 kB gz, CSS 36.29 kB / 6.83 kB gz). No Studio ESLint config exists (typecheck is the gate). Core and shared-types untouched (no test run needed; no OpenAPI/schema change).
- **Intentionally deferred:** a live re-read of the working tree (the view is reconstructed from the durable index, so post-index edits are not reflected — a future cycle could add a bounded read-at-line Core endpoint if a live view is wanted; `getVaultFilePreview` remains available but was rejected as the source for the reasons above); syntax highlighting, editing, multi-file tabs, annotations (explicitly out of scope — not an editor); virtualization of very large files (bounded today by the index's 200-chunk cap and a scrollable container, acceptable for MVP); opening a file view from the deterministic **inventory** panel (this cycle is search-hit → file only); deep-linking / persisting the open file across workspace switches (local state resets on switch, like the rest of the panel); real neural/semantic embeddings (Core `Embedder` still pluggable).
- **Next best slice:** swap Core's hashing embedder for a real local embedding model behind the existing `Embedder` protocol (the schema already persists per-chunk vectors) to move from lexical-vector to genuinely semantic retrieval — the biggest quality lever now that the search→file loop is actionable. After that: an "open in file view" affordance from the inventory panel and/or a bounded live read-at-line Core endpoint so the file view can reflect on-disk edits, and feeding `POST /vault/summarize` into the context-pack/task flow so an architecture summary can seed a run.

### 2026-07-22 — Start cycle 27: real local embedding backend behind the Embedder protocol (semantic Vault retrieval)

- Intent (Core-first, product quality): replace the cycle-24 lexical hashing vectorizer with a **real local neural embedding backend** behind the existing `Embedder` protocol so Vault search ranks by genuine semantic similarity, while keeping the API/schema/Studio flow and the local-first (no cloud) posture unchanged. This is the lever both cycles 25 and 26 named as next.
- Re-read the ground truth at commit `dd47b74`: `Embedder` protocol + `HashingEmbedder` + `cosine_similarity` live in `vault_indexer.py`; the indexer embeds each chunk inline (`self._embedder.embed(chunk_body)`); the service embeds the query and ranks `cosine_similarity(query_vector, chunk.embedding)` + a `SUBSTRING_BOOST=0.5` exact-substring bump; vectors persist as a JSON `dict[str, float]` in `vault_chunks.embedding` (in-memory + SQL repos both pass the dict straight through); `main.py` builds one `HashingEmbedder()` and shares it with the indexer and the service. `httpx` is already a Core dependency; **no** numpy/torch/sentence-transformers, and none should be added.
- **Backend chosen — local Ollama over HTTP (`nomic-embed-text`), with an honest lexical fallback.** Rationale: (a) local-first / no cloud (talks only to `http://localhost:11434`); (b) zero new Python deps — reuse `httpx` exactly like `openai_provider.py` (injectable transport Protocol for deterministic tests); (c) stable across restarts (persisted vectors are reproducible from the index); (d) practical dev setup (`brew install ollama` / `ollama serve` + `ollama pull nomic-embed-text`). In-process models (sentence-transformers/fastembed) were rejected: they pull ~GB of torch/onnx weight, are impractical in this environment, and fight the "lightweight, local-first" constraint.
- **Vector shape — unchanged (no migration).** A dense embedding is L2-normalized and stored as an **index-keyed sparse dict** `{"0": v0, …, "767": v767}` — the exact `dict[str, float]` shape the JSON column, the domain dataclasses, and `cosine_similarity` already use (a dense dict is just a fully-populated sparse one; cosine stays a normalized dot product). So the schema, persistence rows, and repositories are untouched. Cost: a 768-dim vector is a larger JSON blob than a sparse lexical one (documented as a disk/latency tradeoff). This honors "preserve the existing per-chunk vector storage path."
- **Protocol — minimal additive extension.** `Embedder` gains `info: EmbedderInfo(backend, model, dim, semantic)` (so the index can record *which* backend produced its vectors, and search can detect a stale index) and `embed_documents(texts)` (batch, so Ollama indexing issues one HTTP call per batch instead of per chunk). `HashingEmbedder` keeps its behavior and gains both. `cosine_similarity`/`tokenize`/`HashingEmbedder`/`Embedder` move to a new `vault_embedding.py` and are re-exported from `vault_indexer.py` so every existing import keeps working.
- **Ranking direction — embedding similarity primary, lexical secondary.** Search embeds the query with the same backend, ranks by cosine over the stored vectors (clamped to ≥0 to honor the `score ≥ 0` model), and keeps the small exact-substring boost as a secondary re-rank only. `strategy` becomes honest + dynamic: `semantic-cosine:ollama/nomic-embed-text` when semantic, `lexical-vector-cosine` when the hashing fallback is active (unchanged string, so the API test stays green).
- **Fallback (explicit + honest — never fake semantics).** A `build_vault_embedder()` factory reads `MENSURA_VAULT_EMBEDDER` (`auto` default | `ollama` | `hashing`), `MENSURA_OLLAMA_URL`, `MENSURA_OLLAMA_EMBED_MODEL`, probes the daemon once, and returns `OllamaEmbedder` when reachable else `HashingEmbedder` with a clear logged reason. Only `create_sql_app` (production) runs the factory/probe; `create_app` defaults to `HashingEmbedder()` (no network in tests). The index records its embedder `info` in the summary; at search time a **mismatch** (index built by a different backend than the one now configured — e.g. a semantic index queried after Ollama went down, or an old lexical index queried with Ollama on) is detected and honestly reported (`strategy: lexical-fallback:reindex-required`) and served by a lexical re-rank over the stored chunk text, never by scoring vectors from two different spaces. If the backend fails **during indexing**, indexing fails clearly (`urn:mensura:problem:vault-embedding-backend-unavailable`, 503) rather than persisting a half-lexical/half-dense index.
- **Compatibility/migration:** old lexical indexes stay readable and searchable (as lexical); to *gain* semantic ranking a workspace must be re-indexed with the backend running (documented; the required backend is visible in the index summary's new `embedding` metadata). Additive optional `embedding` field on `VaultIndexSummary` (JSON column ⇒ no migration; Studio uses plain TS interfaces with compile-time casts, so the extra field is ignored — no Studio change).
- **Environment note:** Ollama is **not installed** in this dev environment, so the live retrieval-quality comparison against a real model is deferred to a machine with Ollama; the semantic ranking *path* (dense-vector cosine beating lexical on a no-shared-tokens query), the fallback, the mismatch handling, and dense-vector persistence are all proven deterministically with a fake embedder/transport (per the "don't depend on a real daemon" testing constraint). The factory here honestly falls back to lexical and says so.
- Follow-up order: `vault_embedding.py` (protocol + info + hashing + ollama + transport + factory) → re-export/refactor `vault_indexer.py` (batch embed + record `embedder_info`) → `vault_index_models.py` (`VaultEmbeddingInfo` + optional summary field) → `exceptions.py`/`problems.py` (backend-unavailable 503) → `vault_index_service.py` (semantic-primary ranking + mismatch fallback + record info) → `vault_index.py` router (503 doc) → `main.py`/`create_sql_app` wiring → shared-types additive field → tests (`test_vault_embedding.py`, semantic/mismatch/backend-unavailable service tests, dense persistence round-trip, keep API/OpenAPI green) → READMEs + this journal (after) → full ruff + pytest, and a deterministic semantic-vs-lexical retrieval demo.

### 2026-07-22 — Complete cycle 27: real local embedding backend behind the Embedder protocol

- **Files changed (2 new src, 1 new test helper, 1 new test; 8 edited src, 2 edited tests; 3 docs + shared-types — NO migration, NO Studio code change):**
  - **New (src, 1):** `services/core/src/mensura_core/vault_embedding.py` — the embedding abstraction and both local backends: `EmbedderInfo`, `Embedder` protocol (now `info` + `embed` + `embed_documents`), `HashingEmbedder` (moved here), `cosine_similarity`/`tokenize` (moved), `EmbeddingBackendError`, `OllamaEmbeddingTransport` protocol + `HttpxOllamaEmbeddingTransport` (`/api/embed`), `OllamaEmbedder` (dense → L2-normalized index-keyed sparse dict, batched, dim discovered), and the `build_vault_embedder()` factory.
  - **New (tests, 2):** `tests/vault_fakes.py` (shared `FakeSemanticEmbedder` concept-mapper + `BrokenEmbedder`), `tests/test_vault_embedding.py` (18 tests: hashing info/batch, Ollama normalize/dim/batch/empty/error via fake transport, the httpx transport via monkeypatched `httpx.post` incl. non-200/exception/count-mismatch, and the factory across `auto`/`ollama`/`hashing`/unknown/env/no-probe).
  - **Edited (src, 8):** `vault_indexer.py` (import/re-export the embedding abstraction via `__all__`; batch each file's chunks through `embed_documents`; record `embedder_info` on `BuiltVaultIndex`), `vault_index_models.py` (`VaultEmbeddingInfo` + additive optional `embedding` on `VaultIndexSummary`), `vault_index_service.py` (semantic-primary ranking, honest mismatch fallback, `strategy` reporting, record embedder info in the summary, fail-clear on backend loss during indexing), `exceptions.py` (`VaultEmbeddingBackendUnavailableError`), `api/problems.py` (503 handler + type const + response), `api/routers/vault_index.py` (503 doc on `/index`), `main.py` (`vault_embedder` param; `create_app` defaults to offline lexical — no probe/network; `create_sql_app` injects `build_vault_embedder()`).
  - **Edited (tests, 2):** `tests/test_vault_index_service.py` (+5: backend recorded in summary ×2, semantic-beats-lexical on a vocabulary gap, stale-index lexical fallback, indexing fails clearly when backend down), `tests/test_durable_sql_app.py` (+1: dense semantic vectors survive a real SQLite restart and search still ranks semantically).
  - **Edited (docs/contract, 4):** `README.md`, `services/core/README.md` (rewrote the retrieval-strategy section: backends, selection env vars, ranking, fallback/mismatch, limitations; new problem in the errors list), `packages/shared-types/src/vault-index.ts` (+`VaultEmbeddingInfo`, optional `embedding`, dynamic-`strategy` doc; `dist` rebuilt), this journal.
- **Backend chosen — local Ollama (`nomic-embed-text`) over HTTP, honest lexical fallback.** Local-first (localhost only, no cloud), **zero new Python deps** (reuses `httpx` like `openai_provider.py`, injectable transport for deterministic tests), stable across restarts (persisted vectors), practical setup (`ollama serve` + `ollama pull nomic-embed-text`). In-process torch/onnx models were rejected as too heavy for the environment and the local-first posture.
- **Schema — UNCHANGED (no migration).** A dense embedding is L2-normalized and stored as the same index-keyed `dict[str, float]` the JSON `vault_chunks.embedding` column, the domain dataclasses, and `cosine_similarity` already use (a dense dict is a fully-populated sparse one). The only additive change is an **optional** `embedding` object inside the JSON index summary (no column change; Studio uses compile-time-cast TS interfaces so the extra field is ignored — Studio code untouched, its 81 tests + typecheck + build all pass unchanged).
- **Ranking formula:** `score = max(0, cosine(query_vec, chunk_vec)) + (0.5 if query is an exact substring of the chunk else 0)`, filtered to `> 0`, sorted by `(-score, path, chunkIndex)`. Embedding similarity is primary; the substring bump is a secondary re-rank; the `max(0, …)` clamp lets real (possibly-negative) neural cosine honor the `score ≥ 0` API model while leaving the always-nonnegative lexical scores identical to before. `strategy` is reported honestly: `semantic-cosine:ollama/<model>`, `lexical-vector-cosine`, or `lexical-fallback:reindex-required`.
- **Fallback behavior (explicit, never fake semantics):** the factory probes once and picks Ollama-or-lexical from `MENSURA_VAULT_EMBEDDER`/`MENSURA_OLLAMA_URL`/`MENSURA_OLLAMA_EMBED_MODEL`, logging the reason on fallback. **Indexing** with the backend down fails clearly (`503 vault-embedding-backend-unavailable`) rather than persisting a mixed-space index. **Search** on an index built by a *different* backend than the one now configured degrades to a lexical re-rank over stored chunk text (`lexical-fallback:reindex-required`) instead of scoring across incompatible spaces. Old lexical indexes stay searchable; re-index (backend running) to gain semantic ranking — the required backend is visible in the summary's `embedding` metadata.
- **Verification:** Core `285 passed` (261 prior + 18 embedding + 5 service + 1 durable), `ruff check src tests` clean; shared-types `68 passed` + `tsc` build; Studio `81 passed` + `tsc --noEmit` + `vite build`, all with **zero Studio code changes** (proves the API is backward-compatible). A **live smoke of the real `create_sql_app()`** with Ollama absent booted, probed `localhost:11434`, logged the honest "install/start Ollama and `ollama pull nomic-embed-text`" fallback message, recorded `{backend: hashing, semantic: false}` on the index, and searched `strategy: lexical-vector-cosine` (top `src/auth.py`). A deterministic semantic-vs-lexical demo over a 3-file fixture showed the improvement crisply: on the vocabulary-gap query **"sign in"** the lexical baseline returned **no hits** while the semantic backend retrieved `docs/security.md` + `src/auth.py` (1.000); on **"graphics rendering"** the lexical baseline surfaced a **spurious hash-collision hit** (`security.md`) and **missed** `graphics.py` entirely, while the semantic backend returned `graphics.py` (1.000).
- **What improved:** search now ranks by genuine embedding similarity when a real local model is available, bridging synonym/paraphrase vocabulary gaps the lexical model cannot; the retrieval mode and the index's producing backend are always reported honestly; and the switch cost nothing in schema/API/Studio compatibility.
- **Environment caveat (honest):** Ollama is **not installed** in this dev environment, so the real-model *quality* number (nomic-embed-text on a real repo) is not measured here — deferred to a machine with Ollama. The semantic ranking path, the fallback, the mismatch handling, and dense-vector persistence are all proven deterministically with a fake embedder/transport (per the "don't depend on a real daemon" testing constraint); the production factory here correctly runs the lexical fallback and says so.
- **Intentionally deferred:** a fully in-process embedding model (no daemon; avoids heavy native deps); cross-file embedding batching and an approximate-nearest-neighbor index (search is a linear cosine scan — fine at MVP scale); automatic re-index when the configured backend changes (surfaced as `lexical-fallback:reindex-required`, re-index is one click); surfacing the `embedding`/`strategy` mode in the Studio UI (kept out to honor "no Studio UX change"); embedding-model warm-up/health endpoint; per-embedding quantization to shrink dense-vector disk.
- **Next best slice:** surface the retrieval mode in the Studio Vault panel (a small "semantic (ollama/nomic-embed-text)" vs "lexical fallback — re-index for semantic" badge, reading the already-shipped `embedding` summary field + `strategy`), so users can see and act on the backend state; then add an approximate-nearest-neighbor structure (or SQLite vector extension) to keep search sub-linear as indexes grow, and feed `POST /vault/summarize` into the context-pack/task flow so an architecture summary can seed a run.

### 2026-07-22 — Start cycle 28: surface the Vault retrieval mode in Studio (semantic vs lexical fallback badge)

- Intent (Studio-only, transparency): make Vault retrieval mode visible in the Studio "Vault memory" panel so a user can tell whether search is running with real semantic embeddings or a lexical fallback, reusing **only** data Core already exposes (`VaultIndexSnapshot.summary.embedding` + `VaultSearchResponse.strategy`). No Core schema/persistence change; keep the panel layout/workflows intact.

Two existing, already-consumed data sources carry the mode: (1) `snapshot.summary.embedding?: VaultEmbeddingInfo { backend, model, dim, semantic }` — optional (absent on pre-cycle-27 lexical indexes); reflects *how the stored index was built*. (2) `response.strategy: string` — one of `semantic-cosine:<backend>/<model>`, `lexical-vector-cosine`, `lexical-fallback:reindex-required`; reflects *how the last query was actually ranked* (live backend/index compatibility). The `IndexStatus` block already renders the "Indexed" badge; `SearchResults` already prints `strategy <code>…</code>` raw.

Backend-unavailable-during-index (503) is already surfaced by `ProblemDetailsView` on the build error — left as-is (honest, observable).
- Why two tiers: the durable summary badge is always visible after indexing (before any search); the per-search chip carries the live fallback signal (index built by a backend different from the one configured now). The amber fallback chip is the actionable one ("re-index"). Tooltips disclose: semantic = local embeddings/no cloud; fallback = results still work but relevance may be lower + re-index needed; the summary badge reflects the index's build backend while the active per-query mode shows with results.

No Core/shared-types/schema change expected.

A small optional Core add — a read-only "currently configured embedder" marker on health/config — would let Studio warn about a build-vs-configured mismatch proactively (before a search) if that transparency proves valuable.

### 2026-07-22 — Start cycle 29: sub-linear Vault search — persisted sparse inverted index + candidate/rerank, bounded linear fallback

- Intent (scale/perf, correctness-preserving, no product expansion): remove Vault search's sole dependence on the O(N) linear cosine scan (`VaultIndexService.search` → `list_chunk_vectors` → `_score_vectors` over EVERY chunk). Add a **sub-linear candidate-retrieval path for eligible indexes** that produces results **exactly equal** to the current exact scorer, keeping the API, Studio, and semantic/lexical/fallback semantics unchanged.
- Ground truth re-read at clean commit `be5ba4b`: chunk embeddings are L2-normalized **sparse dicts** `{bucket: weight}` in `vault_chunks.embedding` (JSON). `cosine_similarity` == sparse dot over shared buckets. Two embedders behind one protocol: `HashingEmbedder` (lexical, `semantic=False`, genuinely **sparse** — a few token/bigram buckets per chunk) and `OllamaEmbedder` (neural, `semantic=True`, **dense** — all ~768 dims non-zero). Search ranks by cosine (primary) + `SUBSTRING_BOOST=0.5` (secondary), reports `strategy` honestly, and already degrades to a lexical re-rank on space mismatch (`lexical-fallback:reindex-required`).
- **Chosen acceleration = persisted SPARSE INVERTED INDEX (postings) in SQLite, exact for the lexical/sparse space; candidate retrieval + exact rerank; bounded linear-scan fallback for dense/legacy/error.** Rationale vs alternatives:
  - *SQLite vector extension (sqlite-vec/vss):* native extension load (often disabled in stock Python sqlite3), fixed-dim dense arrays — clashes with the variable-dim sparse-dict model and "low setup burden / local-first". Rejected.
  - *Native ANN lib (hnswlib/faiss):* new C++ dependency; the Vault line has been deliberately dependency-free ("no new deps"). Rejected.
  - *From-scratch IVF/LSH for dense:* approximate + k-means build cost in pure Python + recall tuning + bigger test surface; and it would put "preserve retrieval quality" (a hard constraint) at risk. Deferred as the documented next scale slice.
  - *Sparse inverted index (chosen):* dependency-free, **pure SQLite B-tree** on `(workspace_id, bucket)`, and **EXACT** for sparse vectors — so tests assert *equivalence*, not tolerance, and quality is preserved perfectly. It is precisely the "candidate retrieval + exact rerank" shape the cycle asks for. The **default local-first mode (no Ollama → lexical) is exactly the sparse case that benefits.**
- **Why it is exact & sub-linear for lexical:** query embeds to buckets Bq. Candidate set = chunks that share ≥1 bucket with Bq (read only Bq's posting lists — sub-linear in N for selective queries). For the lexical embedder every weight is ≥0, so *sharing a bucket ⟺ cosine>0*, and a **substring match ⟹ query tokens ⊆ chunk tokens ⟹ Bq ⊆ chunk buckets ⟹ retrieved** — so the candidate set is a superset of every chunk the linear scan would score >0, and reranking it with the **unchanged `_score_vectors`** reproduces identical hits/scores/order/`total`. Chunks outside the set have cosine 0 AND no substring ⟹ score 0 ⟹ correctly excluded.
- **Persistence:** new additive table `vault_chunk_postings(id, workspace_id, chunk_id, bucket)` + composite index `(workspace_id, bucket)`; migration `007`. Built **only for acceleration-eligible indexes** (`summary.embedding` present and `semantic == False`) inside the SAME transaction as the snapshot/items/chunks (atomic — no partial "ready" postings), and fully replaced per workspace on re-index (delete-by-workspace → insert). No FK (mirrors `JobRow.workspace_id` precedent) → no cascade-ordering hazard. Dense/legacy indexes persist **no** postings → they read as "not accelerated" and use the exact linear scan (documented remaining scale limit).
- **Query flow (`search`, branch decision UNCHANGED):** still primary (`query_vector is not None`) vs lexical-fallback (unchanged, stays linear re-embed). *Within* the primary branch, a new `_primary_candidates()` calls `list_candidate_vectors(ws, non-zero query buckets, candidate_limit)`; if it returns candidates → rerank those with the existing `_score_vectors`; if it returns `None` (no postings / over-cap) or **raises** (corruption/DB error → caught + WARNING log) → fall back to `list_chunk_vectors` (linear). Empty query-vector (all-stopword query) → no buckets → linear (preserves current substring-only surfacing). Net: results are **always identical to today**; acceleration is a transparent optimization.
- **Repo boundary:** add `list_candidate_vectors(workspace_id, query_buckets, *, source_type, candidate_limit) -> list[ChunkVector] | None` to the Protocol + in-memory + SQL impls (in-memory builds a `{bucket: [chunk_id]}` map + `{chunk_id: ChunkVector}` on save for parity; SQL: `EXISTS` postings? then `SELECT DISTINCT chunk_id … WHERE workspace_id=? AND bucket IN (…)`, bail to `None` over `candidate_limit`, else load those `vault_chunks` rows with the optional `source_type` filter). Shared helpers `index_is_acceleration_eligible(snapshot)` + `iter_chunk_postings(record)`. **No API/model change** (API stays stable per constraint; acceleration is invisible to callers — scores are identical); acceleration state lives in the repo + logs + tests.
- **Tests planned (deterministic, fake embedders):** repo candidate-set correctness (right subset; smaller than total for a selective query; `None` when no postings; `source_type` filter); service equivalence (accelerated hits/scores/order/`total` == exact-scorer reference on a fixture, incl. substring-boost surfacing); SQL restart persistence (postings survive reopen; accelerated search still correct); corruption/error → linear fallback (inject raising repo; assert correct results + logged); dense (semantic) index → no postings → linear, correct; lexical-fallback mismatch unchanged; migration clean-schema set += `vault_chunk_postings` and reversible-downgrade. Then Core `pytest` + `ruff`, shared-types (untouched) sanity, Studio (untouched) — plus a small real-repo timing sanity check if feasible.
- **Follow-up order:** models.py row + `Index` import → migration 007 → repo Protocol/in-memory/SQL (`iter_chunk_postings`, `index_is_acceleration_eligible`, `list_candidate_vectors`, wire into `save_latest`) → service `_primary_candidates` + logging → tests (repo, service equivalence, persistence, fallback, migration) → docs (README.md, services/core/README.md, this journal after). Definition of done: sub-linear candidate path for eligible (lexical/sparse) indexes; API + Studio unchanged; semantic/lexical/fallback preserved; restart + rebuild reliable; tests green; journal updated with the strategy + remaining dense-ANN limit.

### 2026-07-22 — Complete cycle 29: sub-linear Vault search — persisted sparse inverted index + candidate/rerank, bounded linear fallback

- **Files changed (12; Core + docs only — NO API/schema/shared-types/Studio change):**
  - `services/core/src/mensura_core/vault_index_repositories.py` — `ACCELERATION_STRATEGY`; helpers `index_is_acceleration_eligible(snapshot)` (eligible ⟺ `summary.embedding` present and `not semantic`), `iter_chunk_postings(record)` (yields `(chunk_id, bucket)` per non-zero bucket, nothing for dense/legacy), `_chunk_vector(item, chunk)` (dedups the `ChunkVector` construction); new Protocol method `list_candidate_vectors(...) -> list[ChunkVector] | None`; in-memory repo now builds `{bucket: [chunk_id]}` + `{chunk_id: ChunkVector}` on `save_latest` (atomically replaced) and serves candidates from them.
  - `services/core/src/mensura_core/persistence/models.py` — new `VaultChunkPostingRow` (`id`, `workspace_id`, `chunk_id`, `bucket`; composite index `(workspace_id, bucket)`; **no FK**, mirroring `JobRow`) + `Index` import.
  - `services/core/src/mensura_core/persistence/repositories/vault_index.py` — `save_latest` deletes prior postings for the workspace and inserts new ones from `iter_chunk_postings` in the SAME transaction as the snapshot/items/chunks (atomic replace); new `list_candidate_vectors` (`EXISTS` postings? → else `None`; `SELECT DISTINCT chunk_id … WHERE workspace_id=? AND bucket IN (…) LIMIT cap+1` → `None` over cap; else load those `vault_chunks` rows with the optional `source_type` filter); factored `_to_chunk_vector(row)`.
  - `services/core/src/mensura_core/migrations/versions/007_vault_chunk_postings.py` — new table + `(workspace_id, bucket)` index; reversible downgrade.
  - `services/core/src/mensura_core/vault_index_service.py` — `SEARCH_CANDIDATE_LIMIT = 2000`, `logger`, `_primary_candidates()` (accelerated candidate set when available, else the exact linear scan; catches any candidate-retrieval exception → WARNING + linear); `search` primary branch now scores the candidate set. Branch *decision* (primary vs lexical-fallback) and the `_score_vectors`/sort/hit-building are UNCHANGED.
  - `services/core/src/mensura_core/vault_embedding.py` — **`EMBEDDING_DIM` 512 → 16384** (the selectivity enabler; see below).
  - Tests: new `services/core/tests/test_vault_search_acceleration.py` (13 tests); `test_persistence.py` (+`vault_chunk_postings` in the expected-schema set); `test_vault_embedding.py` (dim assertion now references `EMBEDDING_DIM`).
  - Docs: `README.md`, `services/core/README.md`, this journal.
- **Acceleration strategy chosen & why:** **persisted sparse inverted index (postings) in SQLite → candidate retrieval → exact rerank.** Chosen over a SQLite vector extension (native-load/fixed-dim-dense mismatch), a native ANN lib (new C++ dep vs the deliberately dependency-free Vault line), and a from-scratch dense IVF/LSH (approximate + build cost + risks the "preserve quality" constraint) because it is **dependency-free, pure-SQLite-B-tree, and EXACT** for the sparse lexical space (tests assert *equivalence*, not tolerance) and it is precisely the "candidate + rerank" shape asked for. The **default local-first mode (no Ollama → lexical) is exactly the sparse case that benefits.**
- **The dimensionality fix (crucial):** at the old `EMBEDDING_DIM = 512`, blake2b hash collisions made a chunk occupy ~74 of 512 buckets, so "shares a query bucket" matched ~50–78% of chunks — the inverted index gave **zero** speedup (measured). A chunk's stored vector holds one entry per *distinct token bucket* (tens–low-hundreds) regardless of the space size, so raising the space to **16,384 costs no extra storage** but cuts collisions hard: selective-query candidate sets dropped to **~2.5%** (measured 8k-chunk corpus), turning the inverted index selective — and it improves lexical discrimination as a bonus. Tradeoff: it changes the lexical vector space, so a pre-existing 512-dim index reports `lexical-fallback:reindex-required` until re-indexed (self-healing; honest via the existing mismatch path). All 298 tests passed unchanged at the new dim (no ranking test was collision-sensitive).
- **Persistence changed?** YES, additively: new `vault_chunk_postings` table + migration `007` (existing tables/rows/`embedding` JSON column untouched — no data migration). Postings are workspace-scoped, rebuilt atomically with each (re)index, and only exist for eligible (lexical) indexes. Restart-safe (they are ordinary rows); proven by a save→dispose→reopen→accelerate SQL test.
- **Query pipeline used:** `search` → primary branch (compatible embedder) → `_primary_candidates` → repo `list_candidate_vectors(query buckets)` reads only those posting lists → small candidate `ChunkVector` set → **unchanged `_score_vectors` (cosine + substring boost)** reranks *exactly that set* → same sort/hit-building. Exactness proof (lexical/sparse, all-positive weights): a shared bucket ⟹ cosine > 0, and a substring match ⟹ query tokens ⊆ chunk tokens ⟹ shared buckets ⟹ retrieved — so the candidate set is a superset of every chunk the linear scan scores > 0; chunks outside it score 0 and are correctly excluded. Result: hits/scores/order/`total` **identical** to the linear scan (the tie-break `(-score, path, chunk_index)` is a total order because `(path, chunk_index)` is unique per chunk).
- **Fallback behavior (explicit, bounded, logged, tested):** the exact linear scan (`list_chunk_vectors`) answers whenever the accelerated path does not apply — dense/semantic or legacy index (no postings → `None`), all-stopword query (no buckets to probe), a query exceeding the 2,000-distinct-match cap (`None`), or a corrupt/raising acceleration index (caught → WARNING "…linear scan" → linear). The lexical-fallback (`lexical-fallback:reindex-required`) re-rank path is unchanged and also stays linear. Correctness is preserved in every fallback; nothing is silently degraded.
- **What improved (measured, deterministic bench, same data, accelerated vs forced-linear):** 2k chunks 0.14 ms vs 3.4 ms (**24.7×**); 10k 0.48 ms vs 20.3 ms (**41.9×**); 40k 2.18 ms vs 111.9 ms (**51.2×**) — `identical=True` at every size. Accelerated search time scales with the *candidate count*, not the index size (sub-linear); linear grows with N. (A first bench run showed 1× — the profiler traced it to my synthetic index using a bogus `model` string that forced the linear re-embed *fallback* branch, i.e. a bench-metadata bug, not a product bug; fixed by matching `HashingEmbedder().info`.)
- **Verification:** Core `pytest` **298 passed** (13 new), `ruff` clean. shared-types and Studio were **not touched** (no API/response/schema change — acceleration is invisible; scores identical), so their suites are unaffected. Ollama is absent here, so the dense path is validated with the fake dense embedder + a direct assertion that a semantic index persists **no** postings and still searches correctly via the linear scan.
- **Intentionally deferred:** sub-linear **dense/semantic** retrieval (a local IVF/clustering or HNSW candidate index over the 768-dim Ollama vectors — the one remaining scale limit; a coordinate inverted index over dense neural vectors is neither selective nor exact, so dense search is still a linear scan); WAND-style early termination so even common-token lexical queries stay sub-linear (today they correctly fall back at the cap); a response-level acceleration-transparency field (kept the API stable — the mode lives in logs/tests); automatic re-index when the embedding backend/dim changes.
- **Next best slice:** the **dense ANN candidate index** (IVF/spherical-k-means over the semantic vectors, persisted like the postings, candidate + exact rerank) to make *semantic* search sub-linear too — the natural completion of this cycle; or, orthogonally, feed `POST /vault/summarize` into the context-pack/task flow so an architecture summary can seed a run.

### 2026-07-22 — Complete cycle 30: Studio Workspace MVP — repository tree + read-only Monaco editor + local task board + Vault→Workspace linkage

- **Files changed (24; Studio + docs only — NO Core/Python/API/schema change):**
  - New `apps/studio/src/features/workspace/`: `fileTree.ts` (flat-inventory → nested tree builder + `classifyFile` code/doc/config/binary/text + `collectDirectoryPaths`/`ancestorDirectoryPaths`), `languages.ts` (extension→Monaco language id, plaintext fallback), `localTaskBoard.ts` (`WorkspaceTask` shaped like Core `Task`, 3 columns, `groupTasksByColumn`, deterministic `seedWorkspaceTasks`), `types.ts` (`WorkspaceOpenRequest` nonce + `OpenInWorkspaceHandler`), `monacoEnvironment.ts` (offline `loader.config({monaco})` + Vite `?worker` wiring), `MonacoCodeViewer.tsx` (read-only `@monaco-editor/react` viewer with a decorations-collection line highlight + `revealLineInCenter`), `WorkspaceEditor.tsx` (state machine: empty/binary/loading/error/truncated/beyond-preview + lazy `<MonacoCodeViewer>`), `RepositoryTree.tsx` (collapsible `role=tree`, badges, reveal-by-ancestor-expand), `TaskBoardPanel.tsx`, `WorkspacePanel.tsx` (orchestrator).
  - Tests: `fileTree.test.ts`, `RepositoryTree.test.tsx`, `TaskBoardPanel.test.tsx`, `WorkspaceEditor.test.tsx`, `WorkspacePanel.test.tsx` (30 new; all deterministic — Monaco is mocked, no network).
  - Modified: `app/App.tsx` (Workspace panel keyed by `activeWorkspaceId`; `openInWorkspace` nonce handler threaded to `VaultIndexPanel`; clears the open request on workspace change), `features/vault/VaultIndexPanel.tsx` + `features/vault/VaultFileView.tsx` (optional `onOpenInWorkspace` → "Open in Workspace editor →" button on a search hit), `styles.css` (`.dashboard-grid__workspace` full-width + `.workspace-*`/`.workspace-board__*` + responsive collapse), `package.json` (+`monaco-editor@0.54.0`, `@monaco-editor/react@4.7.0`) + `pnpm-lock.yaml`.
  - Docs: `apps/studio/README.md`, `services/core/README.md`, this journal.
- **Data-source decision (no new Core surface):** the repo tree reuses the existing **deterministic Vault inventory** — `Build file tree` calls `POST /vault/inventory`, the flat `GET /vault/files` listing (limit 500) is folded client-side into the tree, and the editor shows the same bounded `GET /vault/files/content` (≤16 KiB) preview. This satisfied the cycle's "reuse existing Core endpoints if available" and kept Core (298 tests) and the Vault UI untouched, while making the Vault↔Workspace link **genuine** rather than cosmetic. Key honesty distinction surfaced in the UI: **inventory** (powers the tree) ≠ **index** (`GET /vault/indexes/{id}`, powers the "Indexed by Vault" badge and search) — a workspace can have a browsable tree without being search-indexed, and vice-versa.
- **Monaco integration (offline, lazy, test-safe):** `monaco-editor` is **bundled locally** (`loader.config({monaco})` — no CDN, Tauri-CSP-friendly) with language web-workers via Vite `?worker` imports isolated in `monacoEnvironment.ts`. The viewer is **`React.lazy`-loaded**, so `vite build` code-splits it into its own chunks (`MonacoCodeViewer` 1.1 MB + `editor.api` 2.5 MB + per-language + 5 worker bundles) and the main bundle stays **352 KB** — initial-load perf preserved. Tests never touch Monaco: `WorkspaceEditor`/`WorkspacePanel` tests `vi.mock("./MonacoCodeViewer")` with a `<pre>` stub (async `import("react")` + `createElement`, no JSX-in-factory), and because only the lazy wrapper imports `monaco-editor`/`?worker`, the heavy deps never load in jsdom. Read-only viewing needs no worker to highlight (Monarch is main-thread), so it degrades gracefully.
- **Vault→Workspace linkage:** a search hit's read-only file view offers **Open in Workspace editor**; `App` stamps a monotonic `requestId` nonce onto a `WorkspaceOpenRequest` (so re-opening the same path/new range re-fires the effect) and passes it to `WorkspacePanel`, which selects the path, reveals it in the tree (expands ancestors), scrolls itself into view, and outlines the hit's lines in Monaco — with an honest note when the range is beyond the truncated preview. Switching workspaces clears the pending request so it can't apply to the wrong workspace.
- **Task board:** a 3-column local Kanban (Backlog / In progress / Done) mapping the 8 Core `TaskStatus` values (each card keeps its exact status badge). Tasks default to a deterministic, clearly-labeled illustrative seed ("not yet connected to Core tasks or runs"); an optional `tasks` prop overrides them (how tests exercise grouping + the empty state, and how real Core tasks will later feed it). No Core task-list endpoint exists yet, so this is honestly local.
- **What works end-to-end:** open a workspace → Workspace panel shows Git branch/dirty (or a "Connect a repository" hint for a non-git root) + an Indexed-by-Vault badge → `Build file tree` → browse the collapsible tree with type badges → click a file → read-only Monaco with syntax highlighting → run a Vault search → "Open in Workspace editor" on a hit → same file opens in Monaco scrolled to and outlining the matched lines → the local task board shows the everyday flow. Binary/too-large/excluded/truncated/not-built are all explicit states.
- **Verification:** Studio `pnpm test` **114 passed** (30 new), `pnpm typecheck` clean (strict `exactOptionalPropertyTypes` — the three optional-handler pass-throughs use `| undefined`), `vite build` succeeds with Monaco code-split (workers emitted). Core/shared-types untouched → suites unaffected.
- **Intentionally deferred:** in-editor file editing/save, multi-tab editors, editor IntelliSense/refactoring, SCM actions from the tree, live working-tree re-read (the tree/editor read the durable inventory snapshot, not a live walk), drag-and-drop or Core-backed task boards, real task/run lists, terminals, and a live filesystem tree endpoint.
- **Next best slice:** wire the local task board to real Core tasks/runs (needs a small workspace-scoped `GET .../tasks` list endpoint) so the board and the existing task/run/proposal flow converge — turning the board from illustrative into the real dispatch surface; or add a live "reveal in tree / open" from the Guard and change-proposal file lists into the same Workspace editor, unifying every file reference in Studio on one viewer.

### 2026-07-22 — Start cycle 31: Core-back the Workspace task board (real workspace-scoped task/run list)

Status mapping unchanged (backlog: draft/ready; in-progress: running/review; done: approved/rejected/failed/cancelled). Docs: both READMEs + this journal after.

### 2026-07-22 — Complete cycle 31: Core-backed Workspace task board (real workspace-scoped task/run list)

- **Files changed (18; Core + shared-types + Studio + docs):**
  - Core: `models.py` (`TaskRunSummary`, `TaskSummary(Task)` subclass adding `latest_run`, `TaskCollection`), `repositories.py` (Protocol + in-memory `list_tasks_by_workspace`/`list_runs_by_workspace`, sorted by `created_at`), `persistence/repositories/core.py` (SQL versions, `ORDER BY created_at`, using the existing indexed `workspace_id` columns), `service.py` (`list_workspace_tasks`: require workspace, reduce runs → latest-per-task by `(created_at, id)`, build `TaskSummary`), `api/routers/tasks.py` (`GET /workspaces/{workspace_id}/tasks` → `TaskCollection`). Tests: `test_api.py` (+4: real tasks w/ latest-run, workspace scoping, empty, unknown-ws 404), `test_persistence.py` (+1: durable SQL list across restart), `test_openapi.py` (path set += the new route).
  - shared-types: `api.ts` (`TaskRunSummary`, `TaskSummary extends Task { latestRun }`, `TaskCollection`; imports `IsoDateTime`/`RunStatus`/`Task`). `index.ts` re-exports via `export *` (untouched).
  - Studio: `api/coreClient.ts` (`listWorkspaceTasks` iface + impl), `api/coreClient.test.ts` (+1 URL/shape case), `app/queryClient.ts` (`workspaceTasks` key), `test/render.tsx` (default stub → empty collection), **renamed** `features/workspace/localTaskBoard.ts` → `taskBoard.ts` (dropped `seedWorkspaceTasks`/`WorkspaceTask`; kept columns + `columnForStatus`; `groupTasksByColumn` now generic `<T extends {status}>`), `features/workspace/TaskBoardPanel.tsx` (self-fetches via react-query: loading/empty/error + status & latest-run badges + per-column counts + total), `features/workspace/taskBoard.test.ts` (new mapping unit test), `TaskBoardPanel.test.tsx` (rewritten integration-style: render/empty/error/run-badge), `WorkspacePanel.test.tsx` (old seed assertion → empty-state), `styles.css` (`.workspace-board__card-badges` flex row). `WorkspacePanel.tsx` call site unchanged (`<TaskBoardPanel workspaceId=… />`).
  - Docs: `services/core/README.md` (endpoint row + `TaskSummary`/`latestRun` prose), `apps/studio/README.md` (board is Core-backed; mapping; read-only limits; "one new endpoint" correction), this journal.
- **Core API: minimally extended, not reused.** No workspace-scoped task listing existed (only item-level `GET /tasks/{id}` + create). Added the single smallest additive route `GET /api/v1/workspaces/{workspace_id}/tasks` returning `{items,total}`. **No schema/migration change** — `TaskRow.workspace_id` and `RunRow.workspace_id` were already indexed, so both the per-workspace list and the latest-run join are cheap. `TaskSummary` **subclasses** the frozen `Task` (adds one optional `latest_run`) so the wire shape is `Task` + `latestRun`, no field duplication.
- **Status→column mapping (unchanged from the local board, now documented):** Backlog = `draft`/`ready`; In progress = `running`/`review`; Done = `approved`/`rejected`/`failed`/`cancelled`. The 8 `TaskStatus` collapse into 3 columns; every card still shows its exact status badge so the collapse is never lossy.
- **Run state surfaced:** each task carries a compact `latestRun` = its most-recent run reduced to `{id, status, createdAt, updatedAt}` (`status` ∈ queued/running/succeeded/failed), or `null` if never run. The board renders it as a second badge ("run: <status>") reusing the existing `badge--running/succeeded/failed` CSS; queued uses the base badge. Chose "latest run" (by `(created_at,id)`, deterministic tie-break) over "active run" — simpler and always defined. No full run detail is joined (kept bounded).
- **What works end-to-end (verified with a live uvicorn `mensura_core.main:app` + curl, no DB touched):** create workspace → 2 tasks → inventory + context-pack + queued run for task 1 → `GET /workspaces/{id}/tasks` returned camelCase `{items,total}` with `latestRun` populated (`queued`) for the run task and `null` for the other, oldest-first, and an unknown workspace returned `404 application/problem+json`. Wire shape matches the TS `TaskSummary`/`TaskRunSummary`/`TaskCollection` interfaces exactly. In Studio the board self-fetches and shows real tasks/badges/counts, an honest "No tasks yet…" empty state, a loading state, and bounded `ProblemDetailsView` errors — no seeded/fake rows anywhere.
- **Verification:** Core `pytest` **303 passed** (5 new), `ruff` clean; shared-types **68 passed** + `tsc` build clean; Studio **120 passed** (net after removing 3 old presentational board tests, adding 4 mapping + 4 panel + 1 client), `pnpm typecheck` clean (strict `exactOptionalPropertyTypes`).
- **Intentionally deferred:** task create/edit/status-transition and drag-and-drop from the board (still done in the Tasks/Run panels); live-updating (poll/SSE) task/run lists — the board is a point-in-time read via react-query, refetched on remount/staleTime; richer run detail or a full run history per task; linked Vault↔task memory (explicitly out of scope). Mapping stays fixed (no user-configurable columns).
- **Next best slice:** make the board a real dispatch surface — either (a) live-refresh it from the existing SSE `run.status.changed` events (`useLiveEvents`) so run badges update without remount, or (b) add lightweight from-board actions that route into the existing Run/context-pack flow (select a task → Start run) so Workspace becomes where work is launched, not just listed. Alternatively, thread `POST /vault/summarize` into task/run seeding as previously noted.
